O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book which is the following of the science of medicine assembled in its fulfillment, and I made the end by my explanations and by my declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete this with your book, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is twisted in our region and is strange throughout all things, so has perished the science and been forgotten, and remains only from the fires that are left over, namely small descriptions in books of the ancient ones who have moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and are closed the intentions and are removed the knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will be able to live by the same order of this treatise according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and came together the forms of cauterizing instruments, and other tools of the work with the matching of declaration and preparation of them, just as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands found in our time, the art of medicine has been extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who enters this to understand anatomy, as Galen says, until they know the joints of bones, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, and marrow, and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of veins, and with them the cause of their departure.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, Hippocrates says that the nose is much with age, and with work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	And so we say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not well acquainted with what has been said, should be cautious lest he fall into error and neglect the wise men; just as I have often seen many who intervene in these things, abandon their knowledge and understanding, and ignore experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	But I saw a mad doctor who cut open an abscess from a woman's shoulder or throat, and cut the arteries in her neck; because of that many blood issues came out so that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a large stone from an old man's kidney; so he removed a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died inside three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have been called to treat this, and seen the patient's condition and the size of the wound, and know that if they had this treatment, it would kill them.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where a lord of our land had a broken leg, and with the break, he got an infection; and the healers who were ignorant of this, bound the break on the wound with tight ligatures, and did not leave him to recover from the swelling, and so I ended it in that way; and he commanded that they should not be released again; and thus he remained so for as long as his leg was completely infected, and his feet came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and hastened to come to release the leg; and when I saw it dislocated, he was in peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption is already confirmed in the member, and cannot be cured; and the corruption will continue to spread through the member until the member is entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another way to destroy an abscess and enchant it, and then inflame it due to the evil of its sign.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer, when it is pure of melancholic humors, it is not fitting to touch it with iron unless there is some way to remove the corrupted part.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is needed that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: to know whether there is danger in many conditions; and I will show you in each one of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For because it is necessary to keep yourself safe, if the physicians cannot speak well of you. If you take up your arms in comfort, and take your sick gently and firmly, and use the better way so that through God's grace you come to safety and are praised; and let away from you the formidable diseases of sickness; and put your arms back on those things which make you doubt, and have faith in them so that you may be able to come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen advised in some of his writings: "Do not take in cure any bad disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this book according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about the fire cautery and the cauterization of a bad medicine, and they are ordered from head to toe; and the forms of the dressings, and the tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the ventouses, wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is ordered and arranged in the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring the dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered like this: first, after cutting, you must take a piece of bone.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also, recalling the work, it is necessary to tell the quality of aid and the harm caused by each type of condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest words and subtle science, and the secrets of response; and many wise men speak about these things and agree on them; and they caution us not to speak so much about them because they are lengthy.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally to all kinds of matter, regardless of the nature: this means that it is useful for hot and moist matter as well as dry and cold matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry matter together, some say that cutting is of great help; and the others said the opposite: that cutting has no benefit to illness except when it comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat or dryness, whereas it should be cured with cool remedies. And this one who says the opposite says that cutting provides great help to hot and dry illnesses that occur in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of man and his moisture is according to the nature of fire, you find that the body freezes.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never by trial.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And no road enters fire unless he who has proven it, and knows from long use the cautery of cuts, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their inclinations and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space of time; for other constitutions we have no fear, namely colds and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, my sons, that cautery is like fire in its essence, and has more virtue than the fiery medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	The fire is simple, and it does not come from fire to any other member except for the one that is burned.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines that come from one member to another by displacement cause illnesses and pain in the affected member; and by chance, it may kill the patient due to its heat and because of the virtue of its substance, unless there has been an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and through great service and study, as is the truth of things; and for that reason I excuse my verbosity, because I do not please myself with revealing the secret known to fire and the quality of the work, which destroys illnesses in the body, just as philosophers demonstrate; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they will agree on what times the cauteries should be done, and select prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all times, because the evils that remain behind are removed by the aid of cautery; and himself, when the cauteries are done for painful necessary hurts and hastens that cannot wait until greater misfortune comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, that they are doing what the wise men say; because a sickness healed by cautery has no return; and he says so; but it's not as they claim, for cauteries are not medicine that changes the complexion, dries out the humors that cause pain, but rather weighs down like medicine for the speed of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and of its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the sickness comes upon him at no time according to his complexion, his living condition, and its virtue; and are assembled in him the excesses through the acquisition of food and similar things, unless you administer cauterization to him when he has little excess and moisture, as cauterization for bones due to pain, and similar things, and this pain does not return; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the backside of medicine, and this is sight; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is considered the backside of medicine because when we administer various kinds of cures for no illness, and they do not work, then we give it to them, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore seek well what cautery is to the rear of medicine, not according to the foolish opinions of blind fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with a golden instrument is better than with iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold, but rather for its purity and the height of its substance; and they said that the levers of cautery do not cause corruption, but this is not true, for I have proven it, and found that it is so in some people; and golden cautery is better than iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And whenever you use an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is damaged by the color of the gold and if it has become cold at once; and if it is heated too much, they put it in the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because of this, we use fire cautery which we have learned to apply to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	or you have ordered this chapter about the head and jaw first, because the eye is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	how to use olive oil.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is done with moisture and cold on the brain, because of the 'soda' which comes from disease, and also for many humors that flow out through the head to the eyes and ears, and due to many pains and suffering in the teeth and throat, and myself as well, all those illnesses that come from cold so much like paralysis and sodomy and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by medicine dissolving the third nerve or the fourth, according to what the virtues and the blood and the custom of the sick person can bear; and then make again the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged, and place his hands in yours; after placing the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and when your fingers come together, if it bleeds from an incision, then take up the cautery called "olivare", because this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the left side with a small mark of ink, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little while turning; then lift your hand immediately, and bind it with bandages, if you see a small bone, and if not, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you before; after take some powder, and apply it to the wound, and place it on the wound, and let it remain for three days; afterwards put on a soft cloth in butter, and leave it until the swelling is drawn out; afterwards treat the wound of the elbow called "tetrafarmaçon", until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they say, when the wound stays open longer, the pus spreads further; and for that reason, apply mud.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that the cautery must be applied so that part of the bone is burned, and then sew up what has been burned with bone, and treat.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the cautery must be applied so tightly as to push into the bone, and so hard that when you lower it down, it goes in just as wide as a spindle that women use for sewing, because that way the humors come out fast; and one should apply the wound long enough before healing.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cautery do not seem good to me in any way, for the fire is too much in some people and causes fear; and it seems to me that I should leave it alone; because the joints are weakened by continued solutions of nature, just as we have seen in other members; and similarly, when it comes to the joints of a sick person, they are weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and nourishing for me, and this is the one I will use then, in accordance with health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all kinds of pain in the head are chronic and last long, he should use the patient's herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, oils, and bandages; and if it is done the cautery that we have previously mentioned, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be aware that if the head of the sick person is of strong nature and not too cold; then cut as we did before that cautery.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cutting on each horn of the head just to the bone, as we previously said, and doing the cautery that is called "vasselz"; and it is in this that one puts ventouses; and keep your hand so that you do not feel anything near the bone: the patient feels more great pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about that later; and it is fitting that the horn cuttings be subtler than those from which one cuts the mobility of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Let treatment of fire cautery on the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head, and the illness has spread to the oil, and the swellings are purged with medicinal remedies, and other treatments have been done as I mentioned in my division of diseases, but it does not help: then do fire cautery according to two methods, that is to say, by application of cold medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of cold medicine is this: you need to apply a poultice of salt, remove the scab and reapply it over the bone as well as the two swellings, and then make a temple or place where the pain holds in such a way that you can put back the poultice under the skin; and when it's been replaced so that the cloth is tight and secure, let it stay for 12 hours; and then remove the cloth and apply hot salt to the poultice, and leave the wound so 2 days or 3; then cover with a cotton cloth soaked in butter until the swelling goes down.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you see it, do this for any medicine that burns as I have written or ordered to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cauterization is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery so that it has this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a clover or has little horn, and in the middle a small appearance; and place it on the painful part, hold your hand and turn the fire lightly enough, until the moistened end of the thread is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is behind, and apply abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After metting cotton in awe of the neck, and putting sor on the left for three days; then I put cotton moulled in butter, and then cure the left with ointment until it is safe; and if thou wilt cauterize this emigraine with the cautery called "cultellare" at all points, and take care not to cover the artery in this emigraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of a headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure headache as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and seeing that cautery before mentioned medicine and iron do not benefit, then it is reasonable to cauterize with the "cultellare" so long as it is white; and so apply again on the left a line of half a dole of lard, and hold your hand once, and make sure you do not cover the artery and that it does not become infected until it reaches the bone; and be careful of the mandible which moves when one eats, and let the nerves not have contact with the maw except the muet (numbness) and spasmus (spasms), and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or when cutting has great fear and injury to oneself, just as if they were experts and proved; and leave the wound open; but I will tell you how to keep safe until the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If the fire cautery does not bring relief to this sickness, and the patient suffers, cauterize the venom in the head just as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two cuts; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from a cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear is painful from cold, and we have tried medicines that dissolve and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pain does not go away, then apply this cautery called "pins", because it is a form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pointing with the entire finger into the diseased ear, or in between the two where pain is felt on both sides, and you move a small space towards the root of the ear after staining it with the signet ring; and after X points between each ear; after treatment let it be so that it becomes healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization only when there is swelling, as we have said in our division of diseases; and do not perform any cauterization on those that come from a tumor and pus of nose.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this semblance of torture that is caused by inflammation, boils, and gargareum of the head, and which does not value, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, and another a little further back at the temple, and the third near the intersection of the two lips; and put the cauterization on the healthy part that opens, and make the point of the ear above a little below the bone of the head, and another in the temple just as long as one finger; and let it stay there until the moistened wound is scorched; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the likeness of the surgical saw that we have shown before, but it is a bit more subtle and one must make the cuts a bit larger; after care, let him be as I said, until he is cured.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and he does not get better, and the sick person has no fever, then let him have four cauteries: two on each of the two horns of the head, and one on the forehead, and one on the "vessel" which we have called so before, and a cautery on the belly, and cure as we said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease one should give the patient large and bitter pills for the brain; after that, apply to the head of the sick person a poultice made from the root of sinap (which is used in treating plasters), and it is the way of cautery: if you do as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healthy like this, it is good; and if not, let him have three cauteries on the head in descending order down to the neck, with space between each cautery two fingers of a big one; and cure as others, and if you see joints being swollen, then let him do a cautery in the middle; and if skilled is, two more above the two corners, and the cure until he becomes healthy; and the cauteries that are called "olivare", just like I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of cold on the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with years and what we have said before; after taking the head of the patient, then let him do cauteries on both sides of the forehead, and one at the end of the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly, and the disease is severe, then do four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let him remain until his fever subsides, and lift your hand; after that, cure as long as he becomes healthy, and it is the cautery called "olivare" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of the seizure
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The physicians should use fire cautery only on those who are spongy, and it is advisable to first clarify the brain with years and other treatments that we have said in the division when patients are great and suffer from many medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot bear pain, he will make gargling and mastication clarifying the brain frequently with bones meat; after he removes the chief from the middle, and makes fire cautery as we have said before, and fire cautery on the neck, and on each horn; and if the patient is severe and suffers, he will make fire cauteries such as I have told to one who has paralysis and softening of body, on the spine at the back and in the neck, and with olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, instruct the patient to do fire cautery subtly according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are superfluities or moistures corrupted and great swelling, then cut fire on the affected parts as we have said to one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the superfluities decline to melancholy and the body of the sick person is moist, then let him drink something because his intellects must be purified, according to what he has before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After reisiting the head of the sick person; after applying a linen bandage well made, in the circle shape, if you tie it around the head; and the patient crosses his limbs, and holds them tightly from all parts; then present the linen, and apply wax of mutton fat old; and heat the cloth temperately, so that it can be poured on him without suffering; after empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool down; and do this to each sick person once a week with another good governance until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cautered while making multiple pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This type of cautery more often infects the brain; and then put a moist cloth over it in butter and pig fat.
de l’awe des eulz	from the eye injury
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye injury comes first by the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and do the patient swallow a medicinal liquid to cleanse the head, and ward off all moisture, and make them sweat or bathe multiple times on a fast day.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After the command tells him to see his head again, and make the cautery in the middle of the head, and make two more cauteries on each temple if there are symptoms from both eyes together, or one if it is only on one eye; cut all over the cautery every vein and artery that are under the wound, and be cautious of any discharge of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, apply pressure to the weak point as you have done.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at incising how to do it; and never has anyone done so over the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	with a swollen face.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the eyelids are swollen and accustomed and are over the veins, or one finds the arteries that appear on the surface of the cheek outward; and we see that it's due to cold inflammatory humors, then do the cautery as I said at the beginning under the eyes: cut the membrane around the eye, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries over the two bones; and if there is need more, so cauterize slightly on top of the eyebrow.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	In the body of the tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit him, then give him to drink three bitter medicines; after the king's head, and let him undergo cautery on the middle of the cautery olive oil; and perform two cauteries on the cautery which is called "clavilis" above the two sorces, one beneath the cheek; and guard the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by illness and moisture, then apply the cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which there are the forms:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see how I make two cauteries on the two sores just as long as the sores are; and do not let go of your hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	one hair that points when it comes out
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It never happens that the hairs of the sores are turned into pus and prick when they come out, and if one does cautery according to two manners: namely by fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and even, then put the patient in his bed; afterwards sign on the paper of the eyes a figure like that of the fuelle of myrtle, and so as it begins with the start of the growth of the hair; then put cotton wet in oil mixed with muscillaige of persillion, then take the cautery of that shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have marked little by little many times, that the skin be closed to the right; and the signs of health in the work are that you see the paper retracted, and the hair lifted to the point of oil; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then put wet cotton in butter until the eschar is removed; afterwards administer ointment until he is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	If the hairs grow after this, and the skin is softened then reapply cautery to the same place, as you did first; and if the hair is lost, cauterize until the skin rises back to its natural position, even and not touched by the hair.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of medicine burning is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a cloth in the shape of mint leaf; next take French soap and vinegar wool, each half a .Z., and grind together well; and make it quickly, if not cooling down afterwards, then press upon the form as if it were a mint leaf, and put on the paper over the eyes; and if the patient is alone in oil only, do so in both, and put cotton wool soaked in oil beneath, that the child's joints may be sound and your two fingers showing above the medicine, and press I point every time the patient feels biting of the medicine, because it bites as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if you do not take care of your soul.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the morsification has passed, if you lift the limb from its bed, and reward yourself so that you see the paper lifted in the same way as it was lifted by force of fire or by incision; and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, then put again the medicine on your limb or if the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are set straight; then apply cotton moistened in butter until the wounds heal, after applying a remedy called "dyafenis" and others, until it is sane.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must take care to guard yourself well, with great caution so that your limb does not prick at the medicine.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If the paper becomes moist after, and they prick at their base in oil, then resume the medicine on that person who has become soft from the paper itself, as you did before; after the cure until he is healed; and this is the form of a gentle poultice.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to these be your pains; do not return to the straight path for one who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of a fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula in the same way as we have said in our division of diseases, and your cures do not bring any benefit, then it is necessary to apply fire cautery in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in a sound position; and take the meniscus of his head between your hands in such a way that he does not move, nor does his head become loose. After placing cotton wool soaked in oil or vinegar on top of the head, apply the cautery which is thus applied: and make it stick to the head as if it were shaped like an arrowhead, so that they may be stuck together; if you see this, then apply it from one end of the head to the other; if you see this, then apply it in such a way as if it were a tent. But anyway, whatever sticks is worth doing for your benefit.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the abscess, if it bursts open, and remove the pus, and dry it out; and if it closes again, then sew it up, and apply fire to the bowel; after applying the cauterized piece which takes the shape of a hot form, hold your hand near the cut with your fingers on the underside of the skin, so that you do not go mad; and place the cauterized piece in the oil fat, and let it decay.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of cautery just at the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If it is not, then repeat cautery once more, and if you need it again, do so every third day; after that, put on cotton wool soaked in butter, and apply a desiccating dressing for the inflammation until it heals, and if forty days pass without healing, he will apply an aqueous corrosive medicine to expose the bone; and heal as best according to what comes into his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a method of treating a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Cut out the fistula and put it back; after that, apply a camphor powder to the incision, because this is its form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	Instruct the patient to pour into the quantity of 12 ounces of poultice; and hold your hand firmly on the affected limb, so that the poultice does not move from its place, until it is absorbed by the blood; for it is customary to put a cotton cloth soaked in oil or in vinegar on the wound of the patient; the poultice will soothe the fistula, and bring health through marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, then it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is advisable to administer poultices on the nose, and return the fistula to its proper place in the body according to what seems most suitable for the individual.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, crevices occur on the lips called "poils", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these lip cracks that we have previously discussed in chapters, and the treatment is not successful, then apply a small cautery surgical instrument according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it immediately in those lip cracks until they heal, after the treatment of ceruse so that he is cured.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula or on the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after causing putrefaction and rot and becoming ulcerated and turning into a fistula; and you treat it as we have previously said, and it does not profit: therefore it is necessary that you apply cautery according to the size of the fistula; after cutting out or removing the fistula, hold your hand until the iron nail reaches the bone, and on the inside the root; and do this once or twice, after the treatment as we have previously said, so that he may be cured; and if it is cured in this way, it is good; but if not, you should discover the root and extract the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	There is no movement of the bones.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, but that doesn't work, then place the patient's head on a clean cloth; after applying the cautery in the form that comes, in that manner that you put a stick between the tooth; and put hot cauterization inside harshly, and hold your hand so the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after release your hand and resume the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with clean water and apply a warm fire.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in that manner the teeth which were moving so are fixed, and the gums are restrained, and the moisture is corrupted dry.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness in the ear, and the remedies of medicine are not effective, then it is necessary to cut according to two manners: and cutting with butter and cutting with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cutting with butter if is such that you apply butter from a healthy person's armpit, and the end in a iron or silver spoon; after taking cotton and wrapping it on the point of a lancet, and the pus in butter boils, and place it on the painful tooth immediately and hold until it cools down; and do so frequently until its virtues come to the root of the tooth, and look if molten lard and cotton in butter boil, and put on the tooth inflamed, and place on hot iron so that the heat comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Instruct the fire cautery to be prepared in such a way that you take hold of a chain of iron or of linen, and let it be thick enough so that the fire does not come near the mouth of the patient; after heating, see how the form comes afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be stayed the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then they raise it up:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery according to the shape you want, and with the power you have:
des scrophules	of scrofula.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are of moisture and cold, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then take fire cautery from the head so that this comes after, and have two openings for the fumes to come out with fire cautery on the other side; and put the cautery hot on the abscess once, or when it is suitable, until it comes out of the font of the abscess; and if the abscess is small then put cautery according to its quantity, and leave it so for three days; and put cotton wool moist in butter until the arrow is removed; after cure let the patient use ointments and poultices until he is cured.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the caisson:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors (frogs) conquer on the channels of the womb and also when this comes from cold complexion, then it is suitable for the patient to be evacuated first by medicinal solutes; after make fire cautery at the root of the throat, and guard that you do not come too near the throat, but rather let a little heat come.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to perform another fire cautery at the joint of the neck and shoulder, where we have the form called "clavile"; and treat the patient as previously instructed until they are healed.
de la toust	From the frost
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of frost are moist and cold, and the patient does not have fever or sweating, and it is an old illness, perform two fire cauteries on the flesh in its veins; and a second fire cautery between the two breast bones; and perform those who are called "clavile" as previously instructed according to the form which is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, perform fire cautery by piercing where the cautery that is called "poins" is due to the form which was before in the illness of the ears; and pierce at every thirty-three points.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment as mentioned earlier, and so according to what has been said before, and if it is cauterized three times in this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because that is lighter than the previous ones, because you do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After that, lean the patient on their back and on their side; after cleanse the wound which is inside the abscess with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, then apply cauterization with two nails, in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart so it is pierced just along the costal bone, and when the wound of cauterization comes together four times, and for that reason cauterization is made with the cauterizer who has three nerves, because the figures of cauterization are thus cauterized; and they come in accordance with the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cauterization which has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and no time is taken to touch this nerve because there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After putting the cauterizer on the perlonce bone with string; after making the patient rest, and not be troubled by the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if the dislocation is above, such a thing happens rarely, then do cauterization on the thick bone of the clavicle, or many cauterizations in puncturing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and there is a hole from the moisture and a wound for the sick person.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When colds come into the stomach and there is much moisture, then let them be extracted to its complexion, and many catarrhs will come to it, and all manner of accustomed cures will not work, therefore it is necessary that the sick person lie on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From that, after the third cautery one I under the spoon of meat by the quantity of two doves, all around the cautery nail, and two more cauteries on each side, so that the figures of the cauteries are at three angles, and there is an equal space between them so they do not touch together when they rot; and let the cautery be made so that it presses both parts of the hurt, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this shape, adjacent to each other.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	If you prick at the fire cautery with a great cautery in the stomach according to this form, and whoever fears this cautery pricks and marks on the stomach as much as you see of the thread; then prick the cautery all over the cautery that is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After having taken the treatment of the treatment we had before, until he is cured.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As to the liver, when it suffers from heat and moisture and great swelling, until its natural condition is restored by the overflow of bodily humors; and those who are cured of this, as we have said in divisions, do not benefit from it, if they should be poured with hot water; for three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, excluding the phlegm, near the joints or on the costal region comes into effect; and between each cautery there is a growth of two doves; and let the cauteries be long in their duration, and press not too hard with one's hand over all the cautery; and only burn the moist parts of the liver; and let the patient lie right on his sides; and if he cannot, so let him rest, stretch out his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you so wish, then cauterize these cauteries with the knife, if you are subtle and wise in this art, and be careful not to burn all of the skin, because you will dry out all of the body; and if it happens that I get burned, for the skin is very subtle near its edge, and the knowledge is necessary to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When an abscess has formed in the liver and you see whether it is in the flesh of the liver or on the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain that is not too great; but if it is on the membrane, he feels intense, crazy pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure wants to treat the boils, it is convenient that the patient lies on his head; and then they apply the heat or where the abscess is, and then they hold the cauterizing tool similar in shape as the boil is.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the fire cautery as long as the veins are dry and come forth from their source, until the wound is all burned; after the cure according to the cure of the wounds so that it heals; and should not use any fires for this cautery except those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And then it can be done firmly, and so it seems to me that wounds should not always be left.
dou cautere de pleuresin	How to treat the dropsy of the lungs.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said to treat dropsy of the lungs with roots of aristologe, in this manner: take a root of aristologe long and as large as you can find, and dry it, and make it as large and long as your thumbs; and anoint with oil, and press it to the fire, and cautery is done between the spleen and the neck, and two small cauterizations are made on descending to the lower jaw; and one between the fifth cost and sixth, in declination behind a little; and one on the abdomen, and one between the shoulders, and two towards the ribs, as far from the fire as is the cautery between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make it open like an odorant.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say an ancient man that no one uses cauterization of fire similar to the razor, and the scythe, and puts them between the ribs, until it comes to that point; and takes away the fire so much pain as we have said in the opening of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear among the sick now, or a death has come, and a fistula comes that cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse, as we have said in the divisions of the cures, and it does not benefit, then they assert three kinds of cauterization that are all good.
