Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one there is that you make three cauterizations, or four, according to the length of the mouse, as we have shown in the division of cauterization of the liver; and do not press your hand too quickly at all the cautery, and let the sick person lie on their back; and another way of cautery is that you scorch the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound which is next to the mouse, or the flesh comes towards the left side, and lift it according to the wound, according to the length of the body, and the cautery are according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to burn the II fingers so that they are perceived by the other part, and then apply hot cautery, and in this way, you will have IV burns. And if you see, cauterize all of the cautery with III fingers.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot from long standing, and this means that it is useless as the other cures have been said.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective for dropsy, except for the method called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your cure does not bring benefit, then it is necessary that you make IV cauteries inside the bowels, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the groin, and two behind the back on the spine, and one towards the belly; and let the cauteries be close to the spot of the pain.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the cautery, let the wound be covered with gauze to prevent infection for a long time, and do not stop the cure of the patient after the cautery; and recovery would be hastened, and the two humors would balance together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery on the abdomen is like that which we have shown before; and that on the back is olive oil, as it was placed there before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in a person who is suffering from dropsy, and are filled with acid citrine, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the earlobe and little toe; and keep your hand steady while turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep into it, as would be if fire were to burn, and thus they should cut according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After do this twice on each leg, perform two cauterizations in each leg at the point of the cutlery; and let one be at the front near the knee and the other behind, in the leg; and leave them to heal for a long time until they form. After treating with the other treatments that we have said.
de la menoison	from the home
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When stomach ailments come from cold and moisture, as the retained virtues and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines are released and cannot be cured by other treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly, so make one grant cauterization on the stomach according to what he spoke of before or cauterization of the stomach, with a circular motion; and four cauterizations at subtle wounds to all the cauterizations sharp, and two cauterizations on the ribs.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, let them do fire cautery on the finger, and fire cautery on each joint, and let there be fire cautery on the stomach for those who are sick with great pain, because the cure is advantageous when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the seat, or one or more of them, and are old and large, and are filled with cold and moist humors corrupted, and have been treated as we said in divisions, but it does not bring relief, then do fire cautery: III on the spine of the back, those that are entirely behind the mucus, small and small in a triangle, and I on each side; and if you think that its stomach is chilled, and the meat does not roast, and swelling appears in the face, then apply a grant cautery to the stomach, as it was said before, and I another on the liver, and I another on the anus all together, and leave the cautery for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure the limb must be made whole.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of fleshiness which is named "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the flesh (thelul), if it seems hot like a scythe, and then put it entirely on fire above the cut flesh, and let your hand be there so that the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, because without pain; do this once or twice, and if there is much of the flesh, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure with ointments profits until it is whole; and if you cauterize a great cautery on a bone, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly healed wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or incision, which we will relate in their case, if it comes to that illness which cannot be healed unless by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is an abscess that has become inflamed and infected with putrefaction and corruption from moisture, if it must be proven to penetrate the entire body, and guard so that you know how much it penetrates to the bottom.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After the cautery that seems like a razor, and pour it into the abscess according to how much it has entered, and continue the cautery until the corrupted body is reduced by fire, once or twice, depending on the quantity of blood required; and be careful not to hurt the nerve that are in question, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula (wound) waits in the body of the testicle and intestine, then beware of these wounds, and do not make this fire (cautery) only on the walnut (testicle), and think they are not in pain; after treatment, let it be cured until it is sane, and if the wound is closed, and the matter is long time dead, then you know that the wound is entirely healed; and if the matter is not dead, then you know that the wound is rotten, and the bone is corrupted at the font (root); and thus as one of these that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of kidney disease comes with great swelling and it does not ease with the help of a woman, then it is necessary to make cautery on the kidneys of one part and of the other with the cautery clavicle that we have mentioned before; and if the clavius (clavicle) burns in the middle, then three cauterizations will be done in line, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and moist from injury or moisture, and the patient holds urine, then do cutting of the fire in the area behind the bladder, where the hair begins at the root, and on both the right and left, each one cut so long as we touch with a finger; and he cuts also behind the back, wherever they have need; and cut according to the shape before said.
de la marris	of the gallbladder
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the gallbladder is cold and moist, and it does not allow for conception because its flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed; and when they come, he feels great pain: then it must be cut around the liver, just as we have said in cutting of the bladder, and also behind the back; and cut according to the shape, just as we have said.
de la hainche	From the join of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous ones come down to the shoulder of the hip, and because of this he moves out of his place, and there are signs that the thigh is longer than the other when you measure it together; and you find the muscles stretched apart from each other, therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the shoulder of the hip with fire cautery similar to a circle, and point in front towards the joint as if turning, so that the shoulder is within the circle; and if it is done like those who have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, he does three cauteries with large olives, and they are done in the same manner as all the wounds; and the healer until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the groin and it's of coldness and moisture, and the sick are cured with what we've said about division, but the cure is useless, and the disease is old, then you must purge the patient of the gross humors of foul stones or other hard-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cut, and the manner of cutting by fire is in two ways: that is to say, the assembly of hot medicines, and cauterization by fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cauterization by fire is according to many ways, of which some are like this: that you cuterize on the groin three times as follows, and then make a triangular cut with great depth and size, and leave an interval of about twice the thickness of two doves between each cauterization, and use olive oil; sometimes it's done in the middle of the groin above the head, because there are four ways according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	If you see, such as the cauterizing at the cautery of the circle that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hamstring; but do it in this manner that the circles contain the entire hamstring, and all the ligaments burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way one does it in sciatique when the pain lies in the hamstring and cannot reach just to the knee or just to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes just to the knee and the leg, he does two cauterizations on either side of where the pain lies, and four more on the ankle, one on the left side; whether it's a cutting cauterization or burning the thickened part. And if the patient feels that the pain extends up to both feet or almost to the knee, he should cauterize there, three points or four, which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	Instruct the surgeon that if it is made more; and if he sees that the pain is beneath the joint towards the thigh, let him cautery with a cautery cutellaire or circular, and do well guard in all your cauteries that you do not make the cautery so hot as to burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you cause no greater nuisance and contraction for the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who had a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they burned it so much that the leg was completely swollen, and the toes as well, and it was clearly and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purgative remedy that caused death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in both legs together, do cautery in one and the other, as this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the wise men that in the fire cautery of the hawthorn, this is the way to do it: make such a fire and let its size be as big as our thumb or a little less, and so they will make an interval between one another, like this - one here and the other there, with space equal to the length of a finger's tip; and so be the intervals two parts, and also soft as nuts, and have a good iron bar; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated so that it is completely red and put the needles inside the sick hawthorn wood, and turn it onto his healthy side; cut once with the cautery and leave for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and let the wound open for a long time; after the pain treatment until he is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its reaction, and if you see few who practice it; for all know that these are good cauteries, which can be borne, and where he is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make an instrument between crossbars in which it comes down to the edge of the wound, and is either made of iron or of fire with a long appearance, and on top there are two, and each has the quantity of the size of a dole; and they overlap above and below, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the fennel rod on the patient lying on his side with one coast suffering, and pressing your hand very much above the fennel rod; afterwards pour between the two circles of hot water which is heated a little by the fire, and let it remain for an hour, or till ten, and suffer the patient the heat and the burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the mordication, it is found just like fire; and when the bites have not passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hunchback of flesh away from sweet wounds, and let it so for three days, and put on balm until what is blackened by the ash be removed; and let him wait three days to rot; and that would be the hind leg's aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread just to the thigh or just to the leg, make an instrument that resembles flesh according to what you have done in the hunchback more frequently; and this is the way of applying a warm poultice, and I have written it in the treatment of rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and live sulfur, an equal amount of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	In case the head of the shoulder becomes dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly displacing with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first set the displacement.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And when it is very moist and is brought to move by the work of medicine and cauteries of other limbs; because it does all sorts of work like fire, and if other medicines are applied well, such as those made from heat, and honey tamarind, and cauterizing with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galen tells us of a cure for one man who was cured of pain in his groin and sciatica, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other cure is needed, and that he became whole again only once when this cure was performed, and then he bathed as he teaches here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	Instruct the patient to grasp a piece of fresh green liver and crush it a little with a few grains of fat, and put it on the groin, thigh, or where the pain is felt, and tie; and let him stay for three hours and according to the quantity that the sick person no longer feels the ache.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is a little moistened, and make him lie down, and the pain will depart entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	Know that no one should use fire cautery on these treatments unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyascorides says that when the sciatica vein is cauterized with horsehair, it will help much; and thus, in this manner, the cautery should be done.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and anoint it with old oil, and place it on the depression that is between the thumb and the little finger, which is called the fossicle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried mutton fat, and applying it to fire until it is charcoal, anoint the linen with it, and place it on the flesh, and leave it until it stains; and repeat this process again, and do not cease doing so until you think that the pain has been relieved, and the cauterization of "chevre" has taken effect.
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or due to great evacuation of blood, or because it seems like the material is spread out cold, nothing of these symptoms is worth cauterization, except for that which has come from an infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be free from fetid pills or other similar things, which are placed on his back, in one place or where the pain holds, three lines marked with an incision, and in each line V cauteries or more according to virtue and quantity the patient can bear; and let it be done the cautery as called "poins"; and if you see, do III cauteries or IV at the cautery clavicle straight according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes in small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow spine when they rise up, and fear; and you will find on the lower back of the spine and on the other spines as well.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and it is being cured, cut the ulcer at the cautery of the circle according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery damages each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that cutting into the spine with fire point to one side and three points on the other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, let him remain so long as he is sane according to what we have said, and take care that you do not apply fire cautery in a ganglion which contains the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by swelling in each limb of the body, and when pain comes to the foot, they call it "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and no medicines can cure it, then it must be cured with fire cautery in this way: make a poultice of fire cautery around the joint on the foot, and let it be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it has need to prick at the flesh of the foot, then pricking with cauterization at the point claimed.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then pricking with cauterization on each knee three times or four times for each part, at all the olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand in fire longer than until the flesh is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knees and back, administer the cauterization as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, prick with points two lines deep; and if no pain remains after this, prick each joint and the skin of the hand; and if pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good management for the patient and use medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If you act well and purge your humors, then you will be healed by God's aid.
de la routure dou syfac	from the cut of the surgery
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When surgery comes with gangrene, and the bowels descend into the cavities, and it is new to you, then it is wise that when you treat his wounds, do not repeat what was done yesterday; and use things that cleanse the belly, so that the fever descends from his belly; after that, seat him on his back between your hands, and he commands that he should bend his knee until the bowels are cleansed, and return to their place, and then sign above the surgery with a certain mark that is similar to half of a circle above the bone of the joint; for this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until he is white and his senses are clear.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then tighten the bowels to their place; and let the surgeons tie a knot in his hand so it will not come back again; and do well for the patient by working on his thighs, and putting in some cassis and servants on his thighs, and another one on his foot which tightens his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of the joint to all your fingers, and your right hand and your thumb until you have pierced the bone, and if you do not pierce it the first time, so that it comes again another time until you get to the bone; and be careful and subtle that the bowels do not escape when you are doing the cautery; nor burn them; lest the patient die, or suffer some other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone at the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is wise that the cautery of children be subtle according to their measure, and as great men as great according to their measure; after three days cure him with butter until the scab falls off; after curing other remedies so long as he is healed, and apply warm poultices for forty days on his back so that the wound may be well closed; and it is wise that his nurses take care of him long enough, so that the boils do not rise when he will get up to go into the chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, give him a bandage well made, and apply it for forty other days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and avoids excessive drinking and eating, and not speaking too loudly; and whenever you follow this instruction, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after the treatment of cutting on its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the abdominal incision
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When incisions come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer swell up, if you do the fire cautery according to its quantity, cut off one third of the wound; after the cure as we have said; for none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark first the left part of the incision and make a line above it for its width, and another below it, and with your hand, cut all around the fire cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, either from a fall or an injury, and this pain lingers for a long time, and the cure with medicine is not worth it, then it is suitable to cauterize with the cautery called "poins", and to cauterize according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed by the first cautery, it's well; if not, do another cautery on that one, because part of the custom is to allow it to change into the member next to it, so that you make cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The trouble is often treated with no success by cautery for a great amount of pain, and in the same way the disease that comes from the decay of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You should view cautery, take care if the disease is in its early stages, and treat it according to what we have said in division, and do not cut or stay, for you will doubt that corruption will spread throughout the whole patient, so perform cautery on the head: I put a new bandage around the head, and another near the front of the hair; and two at the base of the horns, and one behind; and let your hand remain still until the cautery comes to bone, and until the scales come out completely so that the vapors of the large humors can escape; and cut the caul according to what is in front of it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And knows that when you do more cautery, you do more harm, and bring about less profit; and knows that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as they would if they were healthy, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the way of iron tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment let him eat a diet of flour and honey many times until he is restored to health.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation comes into any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and ointments, and it is not restored to health, then you do cautery on the member according to its size and shape, entering a little inside when the wound is fresh; and afterward treat with splints until he is restored to health.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at no time is cautery performed with the hand and foot and back, on account of the numbness that seizes the limb, and thus if it is extracted the swelling; and none of this should enter into it unless they are aware of the limbs and their openings moving the body.
de albaras	of wounds
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called wounds is aged and medicine has no value, then cut with cautery one point only deep enough, according to the quantity of the wound’s flesh, until the bleeding is stopped and its color changes; then cure with flour from fenugreek and lentils with olive oil and plantain leaves, and venison blood and bird gall, each part separately; mix everything together, and bind with a cloth, and apply to the limb till it is cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of ulcers by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the ulcer begins to form and you look at it, stop the bleeding if you apply cautery in the shape of a circle around the whole circumference of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise people say that one should apply cautery in the middle of the ulcer as well; but I do not think this is good, because I fear it will cause more ulcers and corruption, and I have never seen such a case before; and there is no other remedy than to cut around with the cautery called "circule", just like we said in many instances of cautery.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swellings that cannot be cut
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have an illness called "adubelati", and it takes a long time to die, or because of its swelling, or because of the old age of the patient when he is weak (that means too much age), and he has little blood, or for his weight; and you see that you must hasten its death: then apply cautery around with many small cauteries puncturing; after put it so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced with the fire cautery, so that the cautery is poured into this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand at the middle of that ill disease called "adubelati" so that the cautery pierces the vein, and is made such that the patient feels pain in that part in this manner, so that the course of the putrefaction may be delayed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is completely recovered.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else than a wound on the limb, for it corrupts the limbs as the fire corrupts dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a person who can suffer cautery together with fire, then heat the cauterization instruments very small and great, according to what is needed for the patient or where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts until you reach the whole corruption, and nothing remains except that which is corrupted be destroyed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him remain three days, and apply the cauterized sufferings to a broken skin with oil until the burn scars are destroyed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of created pains.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that a healthy child is born, it's good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization on those who remain corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this sickness is sometimes cured with medicine water in place of fire cautery; but fire cautery is more effective aid, and I have already said the treatment for medicine water in cutting: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pearls that come to wounds
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often at wounds by chance a disease comes to be called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a great thing that causes the limb.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And there are two kinds of fire cauterization for this disease.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to say, cauterizing with fire and cauterizing with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cauterizing with fire is that you heat the cauterized hair like a goose feather, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the nail in all parts, and have subtle edges; after, put the hot metal on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the point of the nail; then, leave it for three days as long as porridge begins to come out; then make an emplastre of vinegar and fresh malt crushed with thread, and put the emplastre on the whole night, and the nail will shed and be desracinized from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the patient's limb with care, holding it straight until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted from the flesh of the body, and often happens in hands and feet, so you should apply hot water cautery: and this is how to do it: take a cane of iron or wood, or a quill of vinegar, and put on the nail and the nail bed, as though you are removing warts; and place the cane so that it pricks all around, then pour a little hot water on it, and hold your hand tight, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and can find its way through to the depth just to the root; and let the patient suffer for an hour the stinging of the hot water; then leave it so, and it will drain all from its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So that you can do this after that one, until you have looked at all those who are in the body, then treat the limbs that bind and constrict.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shake with cold, or fever quarter, or any other thing, it is fitting that you do four cauteries over the spine on the back, four over each spine; one cautery over the foot, and one over the stomach at the olive cautery; let them shake, and hasten their health from the disease of the cold.
des pustules puans	of foul boils.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No time does the body present by itself boils or foul boils that come from grossly corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary for the first time when they appear that we are performing cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery with a stick of myrtle, so the point may be seized by fire, or with the root of aristeolonge long, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time do we cauterize at the beginning when they appear, following this manner, and it cannot grow new flesh in front, but is broken up the superfluous thing that comes from it, and is healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the arteries are cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound which comes to the fore, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to suffer stench.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient to apply his own index finger on top of the wound vein, and stretch it out as much as possible without soothing it under your fingers, and let no pain be relieved from there; then put olive oil cauterization pieces small and large until they are all red; then take I, either a large or small one according to the wound and where the artery is routed, and place the cauterization on that vein where you hold your index finger, and keep it there until it stops bleeding.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If the fire goes out when you lift your index finger over the vein, and the cauterization is extinguished, take another one quickly from the cauterizations that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to repeat this one after the other until it cannot be stopped anymore; and take care that you do not burn the nerve which is near, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when the artery stops flowing, one should not attempt to stop it oneself because if the artery is large, one cannot well stop it by themselves unless it happens one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cauterization, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by a strong tie with thread, or by medicines placed on it which have power to stop the bleeding; and it will happen to be tied and restrained as a result.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will provide relief from tight bandages or wrap them tightly around things, or other similar things, if they do not benefit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no other means or medicine available, they must place their two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out so that it is tightly closed over the wound and over the vein; and he should not move it, but apply cold water frequently until it becomes very cold, then frozen and swollen; and make marks in front of those who need to be cautered and medicated.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have said in the first chapter all about diseases for which it is necessary to cautere with fire or medicine, and the causes and forms of cautery; and I placed that chapter at the beginning with twelve pieces, and I will go through this same book by these same steps because one finds more easily those one has already known.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this one, it is necessary, dear student, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first cautery, and therefore you must be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you, do not enter folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to this treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If those who have been skilled in their own disease come to this treatment, for they have lived with their illness so that it has killed them lightly due to the force of their disease, and because of the great severity of their affliction; and from these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these things I have heard which you tell me, and it is said: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you only allow those who come to you in this manner, but put more emphasis on your honor than on your profit, and do not be foolishly weak but rather wisely cautious of what you are certain of, and which you have taken for yourself; and use pronostication and indication in the treatment of your patients to see if salvation is converted; and that will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and remembrance of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lord gives you good understanding and integrity, and if it is your will to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I instruct you about this chapter in this manner, devising it by chapters, according to what is before or after a cautery of fire, which I have devised for you from the chief joint down to the toe, because you will find more easily what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	fill one full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	It is known that this illness comes often in children at birth, and when the nurse strains too tightly the child's head; and sometimes it happens for a reason unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness in adults, but rather all those who I have seen died from it; and because of that I believe it is worth spending time on several treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw the child of that kind because their shoulder joint was swollen with water, and their head would become heavy every day until they could no longer support it; and so strongly did he believe in the moisture that he thought he had died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above his spleen, between the cheek and the bone; and the wounds are such that when the moisture is between the cheek and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you must cut into the head with a large fissure; and so long as it takes two of us to make the incision, until the swelling stops; and look at this form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscesses are larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and you see the signs that there are fissures on both sides of the head, and the water bursts forth when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not stop: then it is fitting to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision remove all moisture entirely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the incision closed with strips of cloth and powder, and applying wine and oil, and letting it so for five days; then release, and treat the wound by plasters and ointments, and let the head be strained larger, and then give the patient dried meat mixed with a little moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look at the size and shape of the abscess, and the assembly of the water; for sometimes it is in front of it, sometimes behind it, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then to and with the abscess, and the filling of the water, and cut accordingly as you have the power; and be careful not to cover the artery; and let a thin strip of cloth be applied, so that the patient may die from the blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of the shoulder
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When this happens with no disease that is called "catarrh" in the eyes or at the worst, and the disease is old, and medicine does not help, then the last resort is to use cauterization with what we cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, since you cannot cover the eyes, that the patient looks back at his head; after he rubs it with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extract the patient's neck from under one and both cloths; then look where the vein opens up, and the two veins are next to the ears, and they quickly return; then sign of the eyes of pain, then cauterize one and both with a well-made spatula, cut off until just above the bone, and so that it is as high in the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, pour out the spatulate under the artery and strike at the top, in the same way as is done to pass through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if it continues to bleed without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not open at the touch, it is advisable to measure the space of three fingers, then sharpen and cut just to the bone; for the wound should bleed so much as six pints, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point without any sign of pus, but rather causes no bleeding, then extract the wound and tie, and the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	le cautere de feu comande au malaide qu'il laisse les poilz tant qu'il soient lons et igals
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When emigraine (or ancient veins) come back and catarrhs are good, because of moistors in tears and colds in the temples and old forehead, and similar things, and he is treated with various kinds of medicines and none of them profits him, so they extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patient makes a small notch behind his temple hair, and listens as the artery opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beat, and is not filled with blood for many people who are too cold; if it is filled, then strangle the neck of the patient with some cloth, then rub him with some rough cloth, and apply hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take out the speculum as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to burn the skin lightly until you see the artery, then take it in the direction of the pulse, and pull well from each part so that there is no remaining thread; and if the artery is subtle, then turn around at the point of the needle, and cut according to the quantity of the two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, do not leave her without movement at all in any way.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And pull the wound in six parts, from one to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie two levers of a double strong silk thread, so that no purulence appears before the swelling of the wound, and appear afterwards with the bleeding; then cut the superfluity that lies between the two levers in the same hour, and then, if you see, pull the cautery to the bone until the joints are cut; for it is a more gentle work, if the patient does not have fever and he has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is a remedy to end moisture: for this is more aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract arteries, fill the limb with wool of old cotton and put on well-made tights; and when you remove them, cure with dry medicines that make charcoal, and tights, until he is healed; and if you do not cut into the artery at all while you work, then haste to cover it by fire cautery, or apply the treatment of lead vitriol and strain with your hand so that there is no blood; and if you do not have this, put wool on the limb as much as needed until they are congealed, and let it be soaked in cold water until it stiffens, and tighten it as necessary; for what is more moist and easier to extract from the artery is to cauterize the vein of this fire cautery with two parts, but the parts should be thick enough to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the extremities are too dark, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have two large incisions one in each, and when you have sewn them together again the two, put hot iron on both so that they come just to the bone, and cut the vein at the two places; and let them be separated between the two cuts because there is no heat from this cautery throughout all of it; and this is the form of cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down into the veins that are under the forehead on account of a severe fever, and there is no benefit from medicine that we make, and you see the face of the sick person becoming flushed, and feeling pain in the forehead as if from blows; and the skin is wet and moist so that the hair falls out, and the papers (skin) are scorched by the heat of the tears, it seems necessary to apply this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the old 'cure contused', and you should instruct the patient with this illness to let their hair grow on their forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and one cut should be as if two fingers were pressing down on the forehead, and the other two cuts are in the costels (armpits) above the papers, and avoid cutting the arteries that are above those areas by the papers; and hold your hand back from continuing the two mandibles, and let each wound have three doses to pass through it; and take a piece of sponge and a lot of drapery for its sake, then apply the spatulate with two parts as this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
