From the cut at the temple to the second cut; and burn all the wound that is between the two cuts up to the syphach (a bony prominence) above the bone, then take another piece from the middle cut just below the other second cut, and then extract this spatulate.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick in the first cut with the instrument called "culterial", and it is well-cutting from one side and from the other, soft but not cutting, that's its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the raw flesh at the wound, and let the cutting edge be soft towards the bone, and prick until it comes to the main cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut off all the surrounding flesh that descends from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous just like the one at the wound; and then do it again in the main cut up to but not including the other wound; and then extract the blood equally, and press out the vein that has been punctured; then put a linen bandage on each cut, covering it with moist cloth dipped in wine and oil and herbs, and keep watch so that pus does not come from there; and on the third day untie the dressing, and apply plenty of plant-based water to clean up the wound, and the treatment with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Do not move your eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a vein becomes inflamed regularly and you see the eyes cloudy and small, and they weaken your vision, and you burn with pain in the head; and the patient coughs, and out of their chest comes a fever; then by these accidents you know that those materials and that catarrh come from many veins, and since which mother is it, if there is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press their forehead, then make a deep cut on both sides of the forehead and another small one.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, making the incision just until it hits the bone; and keep your hands away from the temples that move with pain; when the bone is uncovered, suck out all the blood from an sponge; then sew between the two lips of the incision and put cotton wool soaked in linen; then wrap soft drapes moistened in wine and oil, and be cautious not to touch the wound until it's healed; once it's opened, you must rub the bone so that the pus begins to flow, then treat with antiseptic things that make a poultice.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of flour of sesame and of colocynth four parts, and mix them together; and apply it to these wounds for to bring forth the puerperal fever throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the rupture of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: dust, or hair, or stone from the mine, or similar substance like metal; or seed, as with poppy seeds, fennel, beans; or fluid, such as water and gall, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear either stone or some other thing that does not stick to the ear nor grows in the ear, if one puts the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then pour some violet oil or oil of sagrament over it and extract it; and let it fall apart into pieces, and press the nostrils when the extraction comes, and put a piece of cloth or wool in the ear to stop it up; and stick the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the pain comes through this treatment; and if it does not come through, then extract it with subtle needles, because in that case there is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps through the needles, that's good; if not, extract it with a small pin of thin sewing; and if it does not jump through this, make an iron ring and pour the head into the ring or ear canal very tightly, so that it can't enter through the ring with the needle; then pull out the pain, because often comes forth in this way as we said; and if it doesn't come forth in any manner, take some glue to keep it from coming out, because takes them the ears when they go into the glue; put a piece of cotton inside; then press the glue on the stone or whatever is there, and pull out the pain.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not escape from all those things we have said, then hasten to pierce the ear thus that it may open and bleed; and the manner of the incision is such that you first clean the patient's head, and extract the blood according to its power, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat or where it hangs down; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the bone, then remove the bone according to your strength, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and the cure will continue until it is safe.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that has become swollen and inflamed, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply a small poultice, subtle as this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and cut an incision of that kind.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this cut when you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many cuts; then pull out with subtle force and at the root, as we said, so that the extraction be eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Then in the water, it is fitting that the sick person uses a gentle blowing of condensing powders, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And if it is swollen in that same ear or in the water itself.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she falls through because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If that does not work, then pierce many times according to the length of your hand, and cut lightly; and put in some pins from one ear, and sail upwards on those parts, and fear from one joint above the joint in the ear; and do not cease doing that of joint by joint until the water has dried completely, and so she falls completely; and if you see, then pierce another joint, and burn one of the needles in the ear, and the other pierces of fire above the joint, until it is more dry joint than before; then repeat another joint of others until the water has dried completely, as we said about the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	When extracting the best (bone), if it is of small size, like a pine nut and similar things, cure as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size so that you can feel it, extract with force or pincers; and this is the lighter thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ear, do as we have said in the division and in treating dilations; but if the cure does not work, look at the ear with the sun: if you see no worms, use fine pincers; and if you do not see them, take a thread because this is their form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And so it can be narrow above and wide below.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle part of the head into the ear according to the quantity of pain the patient suffers; and soon they all come out; do this often until all the worms have come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	If they do not obey to come out, so numb the ear canal with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if it does not emerge as we have said, administer enemas just like the ancients did in the operation of vermiform worms, and you will find or treat enemas; and if you distill your oils and medicines into this ear, because there is a form like what you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is of silver or mercury, poured down into the small passages, and above the overtures for distillation; and to press within the distillation into the silver instrument well-made for this, and if you see the rasp and cloven into the point anticipation cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the canal, and let the cotton be in the ear; then put it into the rasp all the cotton, and press your hand carefully until the oil is distilled or just coming out of the ear; and feel how the patient suffers within, and so much that the distillations are warmed by fire like as they are distilled in the ear; and beware lest they be too cold, for the medicine will not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the bursting of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any perforations in their ears; and this same thing happens to adults by bursting of a wound or by burning inside the ear, and such ruptures often occur deep within the ear if it is not visible; sometimes they have no perforation at all, but the ear remains open.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	This one that occurs deep within, if it cannot be seen, is due to poor health in many conditions, and thus you should put the ear of the sick person in the sun; and look inside: if you see pus formation appear, then there is this small spot where the form is.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And if it is redness and inflammation in front and behind the entire area, if the ear does not bleed; if the pus is from a wound or flesh of the ear, if you have fine pricks, and carefully strike lightly enough, until that wound is all healed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the dislocation is deep in the ear, take a subtle razor and lightly cut off the skin around it, then apply heat to the area of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the dislocation and the patient feels pain in the ear, gently pierce it, and keep from touching the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to its size and width, and apply ointment Egyptian.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and apply ointment with rosewater and powdered vitriol; and if you see swelling of the ear, cover it so that you treat the tent and remove another tent ointed in cypress oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat the patient until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If bleeding occurs from the cautery, plunge an sponge and wet it with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments to remove the bleeding, which are in treating hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	from the ashes of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Put on the patient eyelids when they come wet with moisture and are dry, so that you should stretch them out with tongs and tweezers, and cut off with a small spatula from its roots; then put on vitreol, broken.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if not corrected, when the cautery is applied to the lens with fine cautery and then cut after incision wounds, they often repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when those roots are cauterized by fire, they are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	From the grassle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come on the eyes papers some things that resemble grass in form and hardness, and because of this is called "grandine" disease, and it's an assembly of thick moisture under and over the paper; the work is such: take care if the grandine moves from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know; then make them (the papers) wide, then scrape off each part lightly, then take them with tweezers, and chop.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it by piercing just a little of the paper, if not it will bring no pain to the patient; and if the crack is large, if the assembly has a seam, and the cure until it is healed; and if it's small, if nothing be done with force, because the ointments restore it immediately and irritate the char.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Et se li grandine is descending into the inner part of the ear towards the upper part, if you take paper and press it, and let the dust be at some pincers, and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is stretched by the incision, there will be no pain; and when the dust is pressed, clean the oil of salted water, and cure the patient until they are sane.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	The exinch is a fat that gets trapped in threads of paper above the eyebrows, and this often affects children who have no one to care for them, causing great pain to their eyes, and they come with diarrhea in the mornings, and cannot see the light of the sun because tears fall into their eyes; and therefore they sleep on their faces afterwards, and are awake on top, and their eyebrows moistened by that fat, which opens up in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the joint with your two hands and feel something inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient places his head on your healthy one; and then take a linen cloth, and construct a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained within each part, and place it on him; and press with your hands from one side and the other, so that the contents are gathered inside the circle; then make an incision at the midpoint of the wound, cutting into the skin at a width no greater than what is made for a vein cut, and sew the leather around the opening until you see the contents; and in various dispositions, contents come out from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the cloth gauze completely from between your two arms at once, and turn your hand to right and left so that it is evenly spread; and make sure you do not add anything to the cut, lest you become blind from seeing blood all over everything until it reaches the oil.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the opening does not happen in the beginning of the cut, if you prick it slightly at the start so that it appears, then pull it out as we have said; and then tie up the cloth loosely and easily with water, and apply to the place, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break the bow and put it up to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal him so that he is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the shoulder joint hot, so that the pain will cease immediately.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When the hairs of paper are born and grow in another way than nature, and they wither, if they strike their eyes, and cause evil, so that it brings forth many kinds of diseases such as excessive tears and softening of the papers and albugen, till it is the cause of destruction of the eyes; and the cure comes in four manners: either by cautery together with fire, or by aqueous medicine according to what he has before or chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching or by binding, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is fitting that you place the head of the sick man on your healthy one; then turn the paper of oil towards your left hand; if it has changed, it is good; but if not, take an arrow and pierce the thread above; either cut along the margin of the paper where the hairs grow or cut the hair itself, and pull up to the top of the entire paper, and turn it back on the rasp; then make in that part below the hairs, to the length of the entire spatulum, cutting all the way from the large laceration to the small one; then pull out the thread, and put under the paper a small cotton tent and drapery; then sew above the paper an image of encaustic, like the fuel of myrtle, so that it must be made according to the quantity you see elevating the paper, which is cut off at all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Instruct the patient to tie with a bandage of great quantity of paper as much as the paper is softened; then make all along the spatumile two lines that you have signed, and start from large stitches from small ones; and let one of the incisions near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then pour some oil on one of the two angles of cut, then scrape it all; then sew the two lips to an edge with an aglet of one fine thread, and sew the wound, and make the surplus of hair dry on both sides with whatever things glue to them, if you see this being done; and if not, do not have care for it, then let the bandage and hairs be left until three days or four. Then treat the wound with dried and constricting things, because the paper revives at the moment of the wound and assembly, but the bandage is weak (as they said the ancients), and this is work with fear; and it is that you will know the paper of a figure which is like the fuel of mirte, as we have told before, three inches apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off the head which overhangs with equal smallness according to its shape.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the tongs, and they are not even, take a needle or if it has one thread, and sew onto the figure; and sew another thread in the large seam, and the second thread in the small one, and assemble between your two fingers the threads equally; then tie your hand equally, and tie all the skin over which you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and treat until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, sooth with cerote and similar ointment soothing; but sometimes happens that the hair of the papyrus are converted: if you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and both is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the knees is in this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the skin inside according to what I have said, and then make II joints by art, and II subtle ligatures so long as the paper and the skin are; and cut at II joints of II parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and another subtly above what overhangs from the paper of the oil, and strain the two joints from the two parts formed; and leave it like this for some days, and the skin that is strained will wither and dry and will turn into a crust, so that it will fall off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late and you cut with force, then the cure until he is healthy; and when the wound has healed, and if the skin is lifted and no more hair grows; and this is the form of II joints that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to prick with a fine needle, and pour in a thread of soft and subtle silk; then assemble the hairs and nail one by one subtly, and make the long ones reach up about a palm's length; then order in the preparation another thread of silk fine and briefly, and don't touch the chief with it; then put the patient's head on your healthy head; and so expose to the sun until the pricks are declared, for this is a subtle and small work, then prick the needle into all the hunt in the root of the hair attached, and make it pierce hastily up to the natural hair above; then pull out the hair until you reach above the chase, and pour into the thread that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then take your hand so that the hairs vibrate fiercely to all the thread in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Et if the hare is treated and its hair does not come forward with it, then treat the hare below all the way to the root that you have ordered, until the hare comes out of its skin and you see it by the sight of oil; then you will treat the hare and the thread, and let the oil close, for one day or three days, until the hair grows in its place and is born from its chariot; and if the hairs are short, accompany one long hair from the knee with nature's help, and elevate it along with that which you leave, until it is stretched out and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's impurity
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "alacraty" or oil impurity comes in the oil, there are two ways it can happen: one is natural and the other is unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens by sudden injury, or from cutting, or from fire cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the work is that you cut open the wound, and separate the lips, and put linen tents inside, and tie them so long as they are healing; and it is not good to use only things in the cure that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	But if you do this, the disease will come back worse than it was before; but to counteract that, work with things softening such as fenugreek; and let the rose water or honey be boiled, and seed of linen be cooked, and ointments of daquilon are melted in any of the oils, and a tent is put on you, and the cure for this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are such that you must take care to protect it so that it does not spoil in any other form than the one it was before; and all these works that we have said do not burn unless they were directly addressed to this disease, which returns according to the shape it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is under it, truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things; and the way of the work if it is that you pierce an arrow, with one thread double, and the needle in the fat, and you make it pierced from the left shoulder to the right, so that the thread comes into two joints of the fat; then is the fat above all the needle, and the stab up to one span in breadth.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	In case of the sickness coming from cutting or sewing or cautery, it is fitting that you cut an open wound among the hairs of the head near the paper, and according to what has been said before; then sew between the second fingers of a tent, as I have said; and must one do the work according to the shape of the sickness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters make an engine of all possible power in order that he may return the figure to its natural form; and the sick themselves, according to what they need from operation and instruments, and more so in cases where there are many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden movement of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	For this sudden binding has come to hands in a certain manner that the paper above is stuck with white oil, and it cannot move or do its natural work, so then it is fitting that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the stitches should be made, as long as you copy what is good on the stylus fine, which is not too rough nor too thin, so that the patient can suffer neither too rough strokes nor oil stain; and make your incision, from which you scrape off that assembled thing lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it becomes healthy all of that assembly, and no time is wasted in oily water salted, and then lifted with sweet water, and vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and place the woolen oil on top of it soaked in abundance of wool; and after three days use the collier and such sudden things until it becomes healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the stump of oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two types of stumps: one is like a nervous and swollen thing, and the other is not nervous but has a frozen white color, when touched with iron and kept in ice, so that they do not melt; and both have symptoms that lead to the great vessel, and gradually increase until it covers the whole eye and all light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of incision is this: that the patient puts his head on the healthy one, then opens the eyes; and lifts the paper to his hand, then cuts the stump as if it were stitches, and holds it up; then takes an awl, and puts horsehair, or sheepskin, or oxhide in it, a strong thread; and doubles the point of the awl a little, and pierces into the stump, all the way through the awl, and ties the stump with a thread, and holds it up; then scrapes all over the surface of the stump, from the follicle to the root of the hair, so that the wound is smooth and clean, like silk; and sometimes only cuts the lump, and the thread, as we have said; then scrapes everything soft, for which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to avoid touching the scab with the splint and breaking it, and avoiding prickly things; and after the incision, apply a poultice made of broken silk in oil, and let it sit on the collarbone until the next day; then treat him as needed until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	But if the ingrown nail is not nerveless and you cannot push the needle in and the nail cannot be inserted, then this simptom of an ingrown nail is often cured with medicines; and babies will be born like I have told in division, and if you see it covered, apply oil to the patient, and put a light poultice according to this shape.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And if you gently pull out the ingrown nail, and if you see that it is not getting smaller and the flesh is getting thinner, apply a poultice made of hot oil, red wine vinegar, and broken silk, to the affected area until the next day; then resume the other operation according to the same work, until all the bone has been removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no opposition to the oil, as in the case of an abscess, then apply the oil and let it heal until it is well, and then resume work as before, until it is well.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin with the oil is blackened by great annoyance, when the pus forms and a part of it is cut off, and not completely removed, so that no blood comes in; then dilute in the oil a red collier, which is made from litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that forms above the eyelid.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	For some men, no red flesh forms at all, and the eyelid is covered with paper and cloth to prevent it, and appears like a rose bush; and if there are wounds so that the patient puts their head on a healthy one, then work on the eyes, and clean out that red flesh as much as possible with suitable instruments, and hold it tight with force; then cut off the first piece of flesh, and go back to the saw until the end, being careful not to bleed the oil while working; and do the incision in the spatula as we have said in the incision of the ulcers and small forces for that which one fears it will be seen after this chapter shows; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, apply the oil of wool or dilute collier rouge and such corrosive medicines, and put on the oil cotton with linen cloth, if certain of an abscess forming; and if it remains nothing, and does not come out, and you doubt an abscess is forming, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing remedies; then return to your work until it is well, and do so for each piece of flesh that has been treated in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But one must consider that you alleviate the cure for each weak body through its natural way and through accident, in the presence of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see if this limb suffers from the work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyelids
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These veins are red and covered over the body, and they allow their operation and weaken them every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore to be done first that you look at the body, in what vein it is, whether it is thick or thin, and if there is no other disease than the vein; then do this work as follows: instruct the patient to put his head under a clean sheet, suspend those veins all at once according to his wisdom, and make the subtlest of them double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And set two stones one by one according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil around the veins with subtle forces, and sew the wound for a couple of hours after another, until you see remove those vein forces from the oil; and guard that you do not hit the oil at the points of the scalpel, and do this work in the hour of noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only pierce the veins; and when you have done this, distill wine vinegar red and green into the oil to corrupt what remains in the sebum.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to coil all of that in the same hour, then make a plaster on the oil with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are eased and assure yourself that an abscess is forming, then begin again according to this manner as long as the patient remains sick; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	About the fistula of oil.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When the ulcer is called an "arissati" fistula: if you treat it with cautery and medicine using hot water according to what I have said, and it does not heal, then there is an infection in the area where you cut open the abscess, where one must die, and take out all the moisture that is in it, until the bones are uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bones are uncovered and you see the corruption and blackening, if the pus has all the instruments of which this form is; and it is called "asper chief", and must be made from fat into a head like that, and point it out so as with a lime as it is in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put the new bone on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little so that you know that this corruption is resolved; and do this only once, then restore to the place with medicinal excorticants.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bowels are tied and charred, and if it doesn’t heal in forty days, and the body of the bowel is tied, and remains so, and does not renew itself, nor becomes inflamed again, then no accidents happen to it, as one knows it is healed. If this is not the case, if there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to the perforated duodenal region according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone for the second time with iron, and with medicines sharp, when he uncovers it so as to find out according to this form, and let the nails of iron be at three angles, and the fistula be attenuated up to the head just like you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put the bone of the lower rib on it, and withdraw your hand from the wound a little, then turn to the whole forest until you pierce the bone and feel that the patient is coming back as soon as he holds his hand over his belly; and when he heals and hardens the bowels, then take away the material from the belly; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyelids are completely opened and there is no tearing of the eye, nor any soothing, if it is deemed necessary to tie up the patient; then apply a poultice, pour sucre, with ointment made of ice, aloe, incense, and saffron, and then strain the oil. Apply the poultice over with bands and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyelids have need of; then strain it under a bandage, firm, and reapply the poultice with ventouses to suck out further. Then remove the ventouses and let the oil tighten day and night, and if the ligature is loosened, tie it again as much as possible; then remove the ligature after the day and night, and if you see the eye repairing itself, this is good; but if not, reapply the poultice and cloths and the ligature and ventouses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dropping down from a fall
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the injury comes to the eyeball, it opens up, and comes out of the skin like grain of resin, and it is a wonder to see; therefore look at it carefully, for the injury is severe that you inject an arrow into the root of the part beneath this above, then inject another arrow where there is double thread from the eyelid; and pierce it in, and leave the first needle according to its disposition; then cut off the double thread and tie a portion of the eyeball inward, and tighten it well, then extract the needle and apply the oil of linseed mixed with olive oil abundant enough; and leave it until the threads stick together with the eyeball, then treat the oil on soothing things so that the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held back by the eyeball each part in a circle of cloth, till it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes show great appearance, then take the stick in a subtle manner that comes out from under the oil, and run the moisture away from the joints, and enter as soon as possible; then extract as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from under the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness called 'alcunnati' is not cured except by applying the oil-covered bandage, resembling flowing water, but it's not true water; and the appearance of the patient's condition is that you should sit him on a prepared bed straight, then take his head in your hands two parts, and press so long as you see the bandage coming up to your eyes; then fix it, do not remove and let it dry out the light, and observe how the patient is with such things as we have said; and if they do not come down below, know that it's a false symptom, and when the appearance of the bandage does not match what we've said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	if you sit the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatumile and draw up the cornelian on the skin by continuing the conjunctive with the cornelian and the crown, as long as the bow comes out; and when it is removed, if you distill it in hot oil mixed with honey or fenugreek boiled with it, or with honey, then the cure should be done with another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the likeness of the waters in the division, and what is needed for piercing; if it should be done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands cross-legged, with fires of light from the sun, and tie the oil skin tightly; then put the parchment of the oil in your left hand if the eyes are on the right, or in your right hand if they are on the left; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your left hand if they are on the right; then put the point of the instrument into the crown by the length of a thumb in that linen cloth of the oil near the lesser armhole; then carefully push the "almagda" and rotate your hand until it pierces through the linen of the oil, and see that "almagda" is coming to life at what appears as a void; and it's necessary that the length of the "almagda" be exactly half the measure of the space between the kernel of the plum from before the end of the nail; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that parchment by the clarity of the cornelian, then put the instrument right next to it or near the hot oil; then press with one side after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain has subsided now, so he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and the pain returns in the second place, put some force with the instrument, and when it is stuck fast and will not come out, pull it gently by turning your hand slowly back and forth; and then put on a small amount of salve or gemstone oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the oil in a cloth or linen soaked in rose oil and abundant vinegar, and tie it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	And, and those of our time, put on a compress with abundant vinegar.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the salve cannot penetrate into the oil because of its hardness, since there are some men whose eyelids are too hard, so it is necessary to prick the instrument which is called "alberit", for this purpose is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Et perceive donques la conjunctive soulement,
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the abscess is at its peak, that you remove the oil in front of the seventh day, and the advice of him who cures an abscess; and when it is appeased, then release the eye and put on a face covering with linen for one day, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then you go in and out of the house little by little, and it converts into its case; and learn that none of the disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one day came to us who were from the Iberian region, who said that in some far-off land it was done to pierce someone with almagdad [a type of needle or instrument], which causes the water, but never saw it happen in our land, nor read about it in ancient books; and by chance, it might be a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of forms of alum, because they who do not know them see them; and they are made from pure earth:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of a similar subtlety and the back in three times the angle.
de la char sor le neis	of the black earth near it
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are never any charred nests or ashes scattered about, various types, because there is none that resemble scorpions to a certain degree; and some have charrs (char) entwined with many colors of fuse (molten lava); and some have charrs soft as bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of the soft charrs which are not entwined with fuse, it is necessary to place the patient between your hands against the sun; open their nostrils and pour the ash into those charrs, and let them blow out the fumes; because when you do this what you can sustain for a short time on the delicate substance at one end, until you know that that charr is entirely burnt.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	In case of any remaining thing that cannot be covered up, if you bring all the subtle signs lightly, it will not stay there; and if it does not take hold or swell, incising the cause as it seems fitting; and if it is malignant ulcers, hasten and cauterize so that they are not stained and have all their bones, then put out fire or pour oil or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the poultice does not come over and moister comes just to the palace, seeing that it is sane; and if moister percepts as it seems fitting, seeing that there is bone necrosis in the above bones, because the ulcers do not come from cutting: then it is necessary that you put a fil of linen a little thicker than before, and so that each one has no space between them, and put the patient’s chest covered with wool to some strength, and treat the odorant until it comes out through the poultice into the mouth; many times do this like the children in schools, and it is a light thing for him who does it.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct the patient as much as you know they do not have corrupted that flesh, then treat the child, clean the wound, and anoint the flesh in Egyptian oil, and put it directly on the flesh so it is exposed; do this three days or more, until the ointments corrupt all the remaining flesh; and then put a chain of linen some days long until it is healed, and if he needs to use dried medicines, use them; and that's the form of the instrument for purging the head, because they distill oils and medicines into the oil:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is either of silver or iron, resembling a lamp over the top, like a chain, and lead them similarly; and if you see, do the same, making a closed chain, and the instruments be filled to purify the head; hold one hand on the head while heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the shoulder blade over the nerves
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often it bursts at the head of the nerves a disease called "telul", and grows and becomes large abscesses, so much that they are visible to the eye; and for this reason you should make a copy at first, and cut through all the bone, then apply cautery or hot medicine on them; and if one waits too long to do this until it is very large, if it is hard like wood, of a reddish color, of poor quality: if you touch it no more with iron because it's an enchanted abscess, for once cutting it comes in great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is soft contact, not more so than reddish color, and you see how much can be covered, then make the patient empty and apply the copy with fear, and treat the patient with drying and straining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and pierced
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knowing that when some solution of continuity comes to one of these (cartilaginous) joints, it loses its power, no matter how many times.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to consider this when it happens to no one, if you look and see whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then add the two lips to a suture, and care for the patient until they are healed; and if the lips are torn from one side and the other, it is necessary that you scratch all the parts of their gore until they heal, and then assemble the two lips to a suture, and bind them, and apply powder with dragon's blood powder and incense crushed; and put on the powders a piece of poultice of strong or other plastering material binding, and leave it until they cling to it, then care for it with ointment until they are healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the suture: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the hand inside the lips comes an abscess, like grains of sand, small and larger; therefore it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut each one apart, and pick up with pins, and pierce in each part; then apply vinegar after the vitriol incision until the wound is cleaned; and then cleanse it with vinegar again, and cure the wound from dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des sordens	from the noise
