Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are no times when the teeth are assembled at the top of the gums, between the teeth and the jawbone, roughened and painful ones; and there are no times that the black and yellow teeth with points appear until corruption comes to the gum, and they become smelly. It is advisable to seat the patient between your hands and secure his jaws so that you can remove the teeth or the roughness as soon as you notice them; and do so with red, green, and yellow ointments, and other remedies, until they are smoothed out. If one finds what is at the first position, it's good; if not, if he returns to re-examine on the second day and the third, until you have examined everything; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments for removal according to what the work shows, because the razor which removes between the teeth has other forms than those which remove outside of the teeth.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can before applying treatment because it should not be delayed further; for it is a very high substance and therefore we have no excuse to miss the opportunity.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the sick person is constrained to take treatment, it is necessary that you be certain about the feeling of the tooth with your fingers.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the sick person is because of tooth decay, and it is thought to be a diseased tooth, and treatment is done on the healthy one; and no consideration should be taken away from the pain for this reason, until the bad tooth is extracted, because we have not wanted to do that before to these physicians; and when you are certain about the feeling of the tooth with your fingers, it is necessary to scorch around the tooth all the way in a small spot very strongly to ward off the gum inflammation from all sides; then remove the molar with two fingers or fine pincers at first in small pieces until they are well cleaned, and firmly close the fingers; and put the healthy teeth between your genouls, and let them be still if it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth from the jaw in a straight direction, and if it does not break, take any of these instruments and inject them into each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is broken and pierced, it is advisable to fill it with cloth in that place where the hole is; and if you bind it gently with tweezers, so that it does not break when binding; and it is advisable to apply great care over the gum for to smooth out the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient after the pain caused by the root has grown greater and more severe.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Take care that you do not perform as the ignorant doctor does, who by their haste and boldness break the cartilage every time, and bring them nothing but what we have told; but sometimes they come to it because of the roots that remain, or because they break the cartilage; just as we often wish. And when the tooth is worn down, wash the root with wine or ail or silphium; and if bleeding comes, then employ the root of vitriol broken; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of ulcers, because when one is mute the teeth first, are long pointed and large hinges, which they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are large limbs where they do not bend when pulled, and are made of iron well-made, and have teeth to hold them.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays in place during the pulling, it is fitting to put some cotton soaked in butter on the healthy jaw once or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the jaw is softened, because it puts the tongs which are called "algefri", for which the incision seems like a beak of care; and they are made like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots will not come out at all these ties, then it is fitting that you uncover the entire flesh around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is plain, because this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And even if it breaks and is large, if the root does not break apart, this is good; but if not, using all the instruments, because the shapes come after that:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two incisions, then it is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in the region of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles great pincers, because it is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And if this instrument cannot break, and you know how many instruments of teeth are required; and also other instruments that are not counted; and the skilled masters themselves turn to their own instrument, according to what his works and the patient's disease show, because he has in part such diseases that the ancient do not teach any instrument for the diversity of these, and if it breaks on bone or another part, or devours, then you seek out instruments which are needed, as I have told you, and help with gestures, because it is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let the incisions be large and well-held to hold the bone firmly, so that it does not slip away; but may be able to hold and take out; and then restore him with the medicines suitable for this, if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, he will have all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form and the shape is ugly, and even in young women, so that you know whether the teeth are new after the tooth, and it's not quite right, and we cannot put or fix them: then let the line be drawn; and if it is loose with the tooth, take this instrument having the shape, and resembling a small beak, and made of good iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the metal is put a little at a time in the hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears as if we can fix it, take one piece of lime with the same shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Instruct the patient to let his hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are locked
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are locked, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on that tooth because it is sensitive and will not go back in, and you have treated them with medicines that restrain, but this does not work; if they need to be restrained with an iron wire, for the silver wires rot and become spoiled, but the gold does not move; and so whether you use a wire that is too thin or too thick or too small, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are loose, then take out the wire and place it twice between the two healthy teeth, then put the pins between my teeth, if there are one or more, until you carefully go up to the sound tooth on the other side; then continue covering as you started, and carefully withdraw your hand until it does not move again; and let the binding be gentle enough so that it cannot escape from the root of the tooth.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to tie off with a thread to one tenon, and assemble them, and put it between two healthy teeth, and place thus so that it does not bleed on the tongue; and then leave tight as much as it can stay, and if it comes out, or the threads break, then take it up by another thread; if remaining and serving thus for its time, and this is the form of the dens and the figure of the movement of two healthy teeth, and two mangled ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh as new, just like we have said; and do not let anyone who is not learned and skilled come near to make this form of a bone-like tooth, and put it back where the fault is, and tie it up so that we have said; and leave it there and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is the ligament that comes from under the tongue or from nature present at birth; nor by accident of a wound healed. For such injuries you must open the mouth of the sick person and lift their head to your own, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve of the large one, until the tongue is loose from its place, and if it has a hard spot or another wound, so that there is sudden bleeding of the wound, you should baste it with vinegar and cut the big ligament; and beware that the incision is not too deep, lest the artery which is under be injured; and when you have done this, lift the head with water rose and ash, or cold water, then put a linen bandage over the tongue.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If the blood comes out when they cut, apply vinegar to the wound; and if it does not come out, cauterize with cautery, which is good for this; then treat him with another treatment until he is cured.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the lump in flesh, whether it's red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclining towards a sore, and there is moisture, apply a poultice, and make them come out from one side and the other; and if they do not come out at their first appearance, put vinegar on it so that it becomes stained; then return to its original treatment until all is done; then lift the wound free from flesh and sinew, and treat him with other treatments until he is cured.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no time in the throat where mouths are called "godath", and if it's proper to call them "amandres", when you treat them, as we have said in division, they will not be cured, if they are infected with pus of little sense and flesh color; do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is big, do not touch it with iron; for the damage of blood. But leave it as long as it remains dead, then you will cut it out, or it will break on its own; and if it has a white color and the roots are subtle, have prepared an instrument to cover it, but first look if the abscess is calm and has subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his joints be straight, and he opens his mouth and the servant presses the ligature between his hands, and pushes the tongue down with all the instrument, for this is the form; and it shall be either of silver or fine gold as finely as our knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take the lancet and prick in the almond, and pull forth what is possible, and take no cloth from the wounds, then cut at the instrument, for this is the form, which looks like a force; and look at the head, which is curved, one side to the other, and are very good, and are made of iron or honey.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, then cut with the tongs, for this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Instruct the patient to touch one almond with one hand and the other almond with the other hand; and when you have touched one of the almonds, touch the other in the same manner, and after incising, gargle the patient with hot and cold water alternately, and if they bleed, then gargle with blood or cook grape pomegranate skins, or myrtle shoots, and similar things until their bleeding stops; then continue the treatment until the patient is healed; and sometimes, when two almonds touch in the neck, there are no more abscesses than the two almonds themselves, so touch them as they are bound.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess located in the throat, which was called "little sense" or small sinus; and I had sealed up the entire throat so tightly that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, nor eat or drink, and she died after one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had to be elevated two times by each of the two openings in the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I hastened and stuck in one, then the fire burned, and a great portion of bowel; then I stuck another in the other nostril, and it filled the throat and I pressed the tongue; after that I stuck an onion in these abscesses, and cut off a part, and only a little blood came out; and so I removed the conduction from the neck of the woman, and now she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease from cutting away at this abscess for many days; and it kept recurring, filling my left side until it became very large; therefore I managed it and cauterized inside the throat: thus I stayed there until it grew larger; and so I departed from those parts, and saw that God had done a great miracle after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye drops down and it is prolapsed and elongated, if they call it "perpendicular"; and if it is too large and rounded, then it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the incision does not benefit him, and you see that the arrow wounds are healed, and it is subtle, so it is fitting to copy it; and the one that is rounded assembled and is not long; and if it is bloody or of flesh color or black, then it is fitting to remove the incision from the wound.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner in which I have said, of its color and length, then you must sit the patient down in front of the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument that we have remembered here before; then stick a needle into the eye, and draw it out, and cut at II points as I have said in the incision of II almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is fitting that you do not cover more than the natural excess which is outside the limit of nature; for if you do more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incisions of the two almonds, and the cure until she is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of the cutting, it is fitting that you use an engine at the cautery of the fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the fire cautery is wet water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts their head on your sound body, and then presses the tongue with the instrument we have said in the chapter of fire cautery, and mixes it with hot water shoes, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and by using the tip of this instrument, which has this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to apply a medicine on their head, so that the hairs can fall out and lie flat; and if they prick at it with an instrument, hold steady until they stop bleeding from the same place.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery; if it is treated by fumigation according to this manner, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put all or some of them in an earthen pot, and mix well, and make boil; and the pots should be tightly sealed with a wooden instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and put one of the needles into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is numbed; after that, repeat often, until the eye dries, and pay attention not to do this at the beginning of the advent of the hot aposteme, because many things happen; and do not make this treatment only when the aposteme is descending.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and put it inside the chief [head] of the wolf, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the needle of fire does not weigh down the vapor of the mouth, and this is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times this occurs in the throat or with a fish spine, or with any other thing; therefore it is advisable to treat what you can see, and press the tongue onto the sun so that you may see the thing; and if that which does not hurt me is returned into the throat, it is advisable to make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance, if the thing is burned by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, a piece of bacon, a root of lettuce, or a dry piece of bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then pass it through; and when it comes out, he will feel it again, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument from the bottom according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the patient to let their curved instruments enter more easily into the throat if possible, and lift the head higher so that it stays up; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest they die or push the bone into the chest; and make sure that the instrument is moist before inserting it, for this is where the danger lies, and if you insert it too fast or too slow, push all of the instrument into it evenly until it's finished.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the pain in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for the pain in the throat, as I have said in division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look to the throat of the patient at the sun, because you will press the tongue onto the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see swelling, so that it has all of its little nubs, or has fine tongs that are worth to them.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not worth it, take a caustic thread and put it in the throat of the sick one, then pour or sprinkle boiling hot caustic iron on, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patients take water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take the whole glass of cold water, and close the mouth, and let it go in the direction swallowed, and move with his hand often; and as soon as the swelling feels the water, he vomits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he does not vomit as we have said, then inhale the patient with asafetida at the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the ear; do this many times, because it will come out with a stinky smell.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of the fumigation is that you take an earthen pot or it has charcoals in it, and place a coverlet pierced in the middle, and on that perforated side are the head bones of the instrument; then grieve your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the chain into their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just there; and now they will cough, and if they do not cough, you continue the fumigation repeatedly; and the patient suffers from thirst, and eats salty and spoiled things, and drinks no water; and thus it is fitting that they should be subjected to this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument is such that it is cut to treat the abscess, which is seen when you can see, resembling curved tongs with spikes to enter into the throat; and has a resemblance to the beak of a sparrow, and has roughness of lime, so that what she takes, it cannot be loosened; and thus there is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The physicians treat the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses resemble each other, as the memories of both come afterwards in this book, and are different in terms of perforation and size; and there are two types, one is similar to itself, and it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is for those who are in the body or on the surface.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses of the head are different from those in the abdomen, and the abscesses on the liver chestnut are different from those that occur at joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are some abscesses where you should not pierce them until the bone is dead according to its completion; and if they are of those that require piercing when they are believed to be in danger, but do not die according to their completion, like an abscess near a joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joints, and it is left until it has swollen completely, by chance if they are rotten the ligament and nerve of the joint, because this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is at the principal limb and you delay the perforation until it dies, if it harms the principal limb; or if it's at the foundation, if we pierce it so that it dies; then it is not advisable to pierce an abscess when there is no digestion completed, for fear that the one at the foundation will burst open inside and cause a fistula, and it cannot be cured in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is wise that you know the spot of the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, the departure of the fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the swelling and aggravation of the headache of the abscess, and other signs; and it is wise that you make the perforation as soon as possible, depending on whether they are below the abscess or above, where it opens up; and if the perforation is far from the long body of the limb, and the abscesses are in hands or feet, joints, nerves, and arteries, and all equally unless there is no bleeding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who are weak, because of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there is an abscess in the charnel flesh, if it must be cut so that you leave the perforation until it has been confirmed in digestion completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	Because if you pierce it in front of that, the wound will heal slowly due to the venous blood from it, and is filled with much dirt; and by chance, the lips and inner parts of him will become dry.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that must be pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limbs need most.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	It is fitting that you pierce small abscesses, small perforations; and large abscesses, large perforations, and many cuts according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is fitting to sew or cauter, when it has become like the folds, and softened, so it is fitting to do as we make for the boils: and if there are those that are split into III angles, and if there are those whose perforation is like a bee's honeycomb, like abscesses of angles; and if there are such that you cut in one size, and other sizes, and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the skin surface, it is necessary to cut through it plain; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a lot of pus, and you cut through it so that you don't take out all the pus in one hour, but only part of it; then stop the abscess at its previous spot, then do not touch anything underneath; do this many times as necessary, until the whole bowel comes out; in like manner if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	However, you should expect that the bowel will not come out every time with the issue of the abscess, so that by chance the patient may die, and you should not worry.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	So then avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have cut your abscess, if the wound opens up, and look to see if the wound caused by the abscess is small; and if it's a clean cut, apply strips of linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess, and there's a lot of pus, it's necessary that you tie them off in each one so they meet against each other; and if you've cut into the abscess a part of the skin and tied it around, it's necessary to fill it with old cloth or gauze soaked in moisture, and fasten it on the same day; then let the bone and the doctor of ointments until he is cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if they bleed from the wound come to your presence, so administer cold water and ease, and take out the bandage, and put on the limb again, repeating this many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they continue to bleed from the wound, so administer treatment and care, and take out the poultices that I have in my hands in this book, and since it is winter time, and the poultice or the abscess is very nervous, it seems wise to apply tourniquets and dressings moistened with wine and oil; and if it's on a surface, and the poultice is charred, so it seems wise to put on dressings moistened with water and oil, or with hot wine and oil for three days, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and clean it up, as it seems fit, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	In order to know this thoroughly, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des soros	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the head vein is cut off for small abscesses, and such are made as are in cloth, as well as like a silken thread, and there are many of this kind.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also fatty ones and those that are swollen as if they were full of pus; and there are also those which are hard and stone-like to cut, and there is no doubt about them unless the artery does not become affected.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the wounds of the chest are such that you must experience all instruments called "entromissoire", because it is afterwards, what form comes out of it.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, then they open it from above the long bone.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape the surface without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, because it returns again when we leave anything there; then plunge cotton in ointment Egyptian, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply the wound, and let it be until the next day; those who are left through the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton as before, on the next day, and the plaster, until you know well that it does not stay overnight; then heal the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is sound.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscesses hold tight at its birth, so cut according to this form, for a long time; and remove the nails, and scrape off all parts, and put all your cure to treat the side where it is; and if the arteries cause you harm, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with the abscess if it is rocky, and as you cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut above the rocky abscess and the moist part, if it is lighter, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or swellings do not have any moisture, and those which I cut out from the chief of an old woman; and I found the abscesses as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break them; and if anyone had been burned by one, they would have suffered just as badly from one that was stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come to the head or the ear, whether they are coming from the child's forehead or from the roots of the ears, open the wound so it is always done on the most dependent part; and cure as it should.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times they occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and sometimes in other parts of the body, and are very large, and intertwined one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is precisely in its own side, just as we said about the abscess on the head; and there are many similar appearances of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those who have good disposition at the elbow and appear like the color of the body, and are silent in every part and not red as in the nerves of the neck or artery or conduit, and not deeply so, it is fitting that you copy from above, and scratch from each part, and let the two lips be like the skin around the knee if you have need, as we have said about the incision on the head; and press little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and do not prick with the sharp needle or make thrusts, lest your hand fail, and you see too far ahead, so that you may not cover more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cover the vein or artery, and it does not allow this, apply vitriol to the wound, or any powder that remains blood, and bind the wound; and let it be as long as the incision is made, until the swelling is reduced and the pain of the wound is mollified, and begin to clean.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is not closed, so that it returns to its place, until you complete it; then look for an index of his should he remain with small boils, if they burst and swell.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	But if there is a great quantity of pus at the root of the boil, it is not advisable to only cut that boil at its root, but rather tie with a strong double thread and let it fall away without causing harm; then apply the wound with Egyptian ointment and treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire boil, it is advisable that you assemble both lips of the wound, and now sew them up, so that there remains no more superfluity due to the large size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is advisable to understand how to tie the root of it, and to apply ointment, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scropholes that are swollen with superfluity, perforate them in where they are opened; and perforate them thus as the one said before, depending on it, then apply ointments and similar things, so that what remains of corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleansed, if the ointment is applied to the char, until it is healed.
de squinance	of weakness
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who did it, and that's the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	Those who have weakness, it is necessary that the rupture of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided; and do not make aid for this one, because all the veins and the worms in the mouth or in the throat or both are at those who have a swollen abscess.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When illness is in the throat from tonsil, it must be covered with the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four of a small cut through, between two circles or according to the size of the cut through the sinus, not in the cartilage; and thus this is most convenient for cutting the epiglottis so that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long in length from that.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cuts the mark as far as it comes to the vein; and stops the vessels of blood, so that you see anything, and then cuts the sinus, just as we have said; and is shown by the section of the vein in the neck which bursts forth from the broken place, and by the failure of the voice; and leaves the wound covered with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is past by which one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound from which blood has flowed, and press all the soul towards the cartilage; then administer medicines that give birth to flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But only if the person has swallowed something at such an advanced stage will they be deemed dead, and their skin will be completely dry.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And so they sew the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and the ancients command to leave the wound covered for as long as the malady's poison has not passed, which passes in three days or four days, and then they ordered them to sew the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took out a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the neck skin; and I was called to cure her, and found her dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I realized that she hadn’t cut herself on the vein nor through any other part, but rather came to be so by the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed and sewed the wound, and cured her so much that she became well; and it happened to that young lady only that she turned red in the throat, and returned after getting her strength back; for this I say that there is no fear regarding the larynx.
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This is an abnormal swelling that is called "hernia of the neck," and it is a large swelling in the color of jasper, and it occurs especially in women; and there are two kinds: natural and acquired; or naturally it has no source.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the acquired kind is according to two manners: because one is like fatness in us, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be treated with hot fires except for this little one, whom he proves and searches through all the interior; if you find it as fat as we are, and it has no opening, then strike it as you strike us, and extract it to its full extent, if there is any of it left; and search thoroughly, and treat him as needed, until he becomes completely whole.
des nous	From us

de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division of these dropsy symptoms and how the assembly of water is made and the signs of each symptom, and the treatment that is done by medicine, and the one that is cured with iron: since it is exposed alone; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: this means tympanites and dysentery, because it's a mortal thing; therefore when you do medicine for this dropsy similarity called "exposed" by medicine, and if the cure does not profit, look at the patient if they are weak or if they have another illness than dropsy, as in constipation and solution of the abdomen and similar things; one should not touch with iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient with great vigor and they only have dropsy alone and they are neither too skinny nor too old, do this: lift the patient straight up under your hands, and the ministrants press the belly towards the bottom of the stomach, pushing out the water to the lowest part of the intestines, then take a spatumile with the thorny end in that shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so are cuts made from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Let it be cut at a point, and let there be no entry more than one, lest it may come to the intestine when you put it in, and cannot be closed; then look if the drop of blood is flowing towards the intestines: if it is necessary to split open on the right side of the third part of the artery, do so below from above, towards the bone; and if it is due to liver disease, if it is to the left, do so; and if it is due to gallstones, if it is to the right, let not the patient lie still in that wound lest the overflow flows to the weak place again; then cut all the skin with the instrument, and drink, and hold fast your hand on the entire length between the skin and the sac, as when you scrape at the quantity of an inch or less; then cut the sac until the skin comes loose, which is the mark of the medicine, then take it out, and drink this instrument, for its form is such
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it appears like a chain of silver thin, and is made of iron or iron rod light, and has a small hole in that place; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other side, and one more so that; and the head is cut as if it were a pen, and this is the shape of the incision which the writers cut like a pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is the alembic, if when the contents come to the water, now draw them up onto the instrument; empty then the half or third part, because if you empty more than it should in that hour, by chance he may die from the resolution of his spirit with the arm, or his palms will be drawn out, or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of his virtue signify for the sick person, and their feet; then draw the instrument and hold onto the water, because it is held now by the cauterized spot on the syphac, as I said, so you should pierce according to this manner; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering that, and take a small quantity of water from it; do this one day, and beware not to fall into foolishness until he does not remain but for a little more of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient, and let them drink a lot of water, then the physician should give them sepulture or hot sand, and they should bathe for a long time or by sun, and if they vomit; and the physician should dry out the medicines desiccatives until they are cured, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of hemorrhaging from the genitals
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There is no child born who has not had a wart on the genitals at all, or if there are warts they are small, or they are not where they should be.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is thought that they can be pierced all at once, not being able to pierce the sensitive part very subtle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Instruct the patient to put in the puncture of fire at the spot where it enters through skin and flesh, and tie and keep thus for three or four days until he makes urine, and if a clot forms, cut it off and make urine again, and then put him back; but by chance, if no urine comes out, because the urine that is coming forth does not allow the clot to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For this type of wound, if the puncture is at the foot, it is treated in the same way as we said, because it will get larger.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the puncture in their own place are blacked, because no one is born who has a puncture at the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate until they straighten up their penis; and they can not defecate because the matter cannot come just to the anus, and this is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to lie on his back, and let the head of the rod be placed between his ribs and the belly, just like you would place the tip of a reed; so that the broken piece is at the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which often comes from this, and if there is any, stop the flow of blood and cure the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of swellings in the rod.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes cysts form in the rod, and it appears as a ugly swelling; and some are malignant, while others are not; therefore you must prick them at one point with great subtlety, cut them out, and clean all of them, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and cure with the diafinicon salve until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the ulcer is of a bad color and has pus, it is advisable to apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have applied it, and if the ulcer is in a bad state, with pus inside and outside the skin, it is advisable to remove the ulcer that is within first; and when it is dressed, avoid the open wound.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	But when you are treating the whole area, if it is not certain that the joint of the vein is fully closed, and black spots and corruption appear on the vein, and also on the flesh; then cut out all the black and corrupted parts; and cover with a poultice made of honey and flour, which is made from the rind of quinces and vinegar, and then cure other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if they come to bleed, then apply lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is used in two ways: it means to cut at the moment of bleeding and when corruption occurs; and if the head of the penis is corroded and retracted, then you should pour or apply a poultice made from the penis into the wound, and when the hairs are dry on the tip of the penis which has not been circumcised, or it is caused by a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with an instrument called "chevillet" until the ligaments are loosened and the head of the penis is delivered from all parts; and if this is a painful thing to do, then you should scrape it with a poultice made from spatulle (a type of dressing) soaked in water, which will not stick directly.
de la circoncision	About circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a cause of continuing the wound like other cuts; any way we make this work by our willpower, and especially in children, since it is necessary that we do the better work, and the lighter to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say that they cut their children's circumcision, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have sought the most important part of the masters and healers who practiced circumcision, such as those in Italy, who were skilled, and all had a new method; because they feared the knives because it had two edges, and by chance some got cut above and below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	For the recovery, and it is double pain, and at the purification which is not certain with the point of the limb; and by chance, the wire escapes the iron, and the wound heals, and many times as if they did not need a purification, and I have wanted to.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is made with force all along the thread of the line I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly as well above as below.
