Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, the force cuts equally above and below all; but if the thread is properly stretched within the leather; and if the manner of the first operation is such that you will make the child think, if it feels, that you are only tying the thread around the handle so tightly, and doing so in all sorts of ways; then you will make it straight between your hands, and release the forces between your hands or on either side your feet that the child does not see, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the handle and blow upon it, and draw it up as much as possible so that the head of the handle is clear; then purify it well from the dirt that is assembled there; then tie a double thread to it; tie it below one another; and hold two threads like this for two times with the pouchet and the doigt, and cut between the two tied threads; and draw the wound above hastily and pull up the head of the handle; then let the blood flow little by little, because that is the best; and put powder on it and on top of it the powdered rose-glue made from a moist mixture of milk cooked with rose water, congealed with good olive oil and fresh, and leave it so for another day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the powers at purification is this: the two shoulders are tied and pressed, and the shoulders should be equally heavy as the arms.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the key (or vein) is found within the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend to your angle, so that the abscesses be made; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold to your angle, then take a nail, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it remains three days, and the part beneath the vein is swollen, you should leave it until the abscesses are brought to a head, and scorch lightly; cut as you can, and be careful of the part of the vein, so that it will not harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the wounded limb of sudden injury, like we have said when treating poudres, and if it is struck with excessive force, and it goes to the top, so that it does not cause harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is whole again.
dou retenement de l’urine	about the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to stone obstruction, or blood clotting, or bowel blockage, or gallstones, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see it is blocked by a stone which lies near or over the neck of the bladder, it is wise to let the patient lean on his knees; and they should place the feet on their backs, and extend his belly from the top of the back, and restrain the patient so that he does not urinate as long as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone above, for this reason the urine flows freely; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is wise to administer extraction to all the instruments called "siringue", such as silver wire thin and lightweight like a bird's feather, with a cane of half a palm long and subtle at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, and tie to the head one thread of flax or linen, and drink from the head through a tube; and press the overflow of the linen and put it into the head of the tube, then anoint the tube with oil or butter and vinegar, and make the patient sit on the bed, and tie the bladder and the prostate with moist oil and olive oil and water; then gently place the tube in the prostate, until it reaches the root of the prostate, then double the prostate over against the bone; then drink from the tube before it reaches the bladder, and feel the malady come to the empty thing, and that is not made according to this order because the direction through which it goes is twisted; then tie the thread with all the flax slowly and slowly, and follow the urine, then extract it, and make the urine flow; and reinsert the tube until the bladder is empty, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or ulcers come to the bladder, or when putrefaction is assembled, and you see water and medicine distilled from it, do this with all the instrument called "clepsedre", and that is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if it has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and put the medicinal poultice in a way that sooths well the tip of the penis until we can treat the moisture, and push out whenever necessary; and when you see your medicines flowing into the bladder, place the chief instrument in the moisture, and pull it up with the one attached to it; if you pull up the moisture from the instrument, then it will enter the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of subtle cathetering which we catheterize the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et est d'argent ou d'archaut, and it is the key which is higher; and below it there are two joints where the joints stick; then take a sheep's bladder vessel and put in the moisture that you see clumping up the vessel, then tie between the two shoulders with a good double thread, and heat it over the fire; then pour the head into the slit in the vessel, then strain your hand on the vessel immediately, until the patient feels that this moisture has come to the vessel; and if you don't have the vessel, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and round it completely around; then pour the strong thread into those holes, then assemble the circle as we assemble the nail, and put in what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do so as you have done with the vessel, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the vessel.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division of stones the ways of cutting stones and extracting medicines; and I told you about the difference between a stone that is hard as rain and all signs, and where to operate on it, whether on the belly or on the phallus; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder often happens to children, and this is a sign that the water burst forth from the bladder like water from its subtlety; and they open a wound, and scratch their patients' genitals, and prick them many times, and then enrage them; and because of these injuries, there are many deaths; and the healing of children until they are 4 years old is much lighter, and it is very painful in the elderly, and it falls into one type, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is fitting first to cleanse the patient with a catheter, so that all the filth within the bowels may be removed.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it is not needed to inquire about cutting into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and bound and move downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not slide up with him at all; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his feet should be below his crotch, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; then ask and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now and cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out at the toucher to the full, apply to your right index finger with oil from your left hand, whether the patient is sick or if he is a youth accomplished; and pour into its base, and ask for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, if it is smooth at the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and pour out to where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and he is commanded to stretch out both hands, one with the fingers in the upper part, and with the other hand he loosens the skin that is under the fingers in the part where they make the operation; then he pours the spatumile by cutting, because this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they put what is between the fingers and the foundation not in the middle but on the left side of the skin; and it should be straight above the stone, and his two hands should meet at the foundation, and they should cut through the notch so that it is wide enough to avoid, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, if the pressure causes a bone on the foundation to break, it will fall out in the work; and observe which there is more stone or angles, and edges: if it sticks to come out; and if there is part that is soft, like a nailhead, and rounded, from which the issue comes light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For the angles and margin of this body, make the cut larger; and if it does not leap, so as to fit in the nails that are as sharp as a file on the head, to press out the stone so that it does not escape; or you pour into the instrument, curved at the top, under the head; and if you cannot do this, then enlarge the pit, and if it is not cleaned, strain with vitriol; and if there are more stones, first pour in the largest one near the bladder's neck, then cut on it, then pull out, and the smaller ones afterwards, if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, so as to sew, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Because two things happen to the patient: either they die, or their urine comes up again after the wound has been sewn; but in any case, you must try to treat, or to remove the nails, as much as possible until you have completed your work; and when you have finished, apply the plaster of encephalitis, aloes, and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put a wet cloth above with olive oil and vinegar, or with olive oil and rosewater and cold water to calm the abscess; then revive the patient on his back, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, so that the limb is well-oiled with oil and water, then apply ointment of defyingfincon and ointment of basilicon, until it is well-healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes to the wound and causes corrosion, and freezing of blood in the bladder, and it prevents the urine from being released, which is done in this way that without purging with the urine: put then your poultice on the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains there, the bladder will freeze and destroy; then raise the wound with water and ash and wool, and aid him in all ways that you know, until he is well-healed; and it is fitting that every treatment you apply to him, you tie his two legs together, and assemble the medicines above the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small and it's lodged in the urethra and fixed there, and urine cannot come out; then, if you follow what I've said, cutting off the tail is excused by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried that way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron according to this form and put three nails at one angle in the bone.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the urethra under the stone, so that it cannot come out afterwards in the bladder; then put the iron into the urethra lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron to your hand on the bone little by little, until you can pierce the bone from the other side; when it comes at once, then press your hand over the part that remains of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken so that urine flows out with the breakage and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie the thread under the bone and the other above, then make the rod straight into the bone between the two joints, then pull it out, and free the joint, and clean the wound with ice on the sore that was in the injury; and cure so long as he is sane.
de la piere des femmes	of a woman's bone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is little chance that a bone will become incarcerated in women, and if it does happen, the cure is painful, and is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is virgin; and the second is that no one can find a woman who knows how to clean herself properly, especially when she is menstruating.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	For the third manner, it is so that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and for the fourth manner, the thigh of the woman is more suited to be operated on than the man's, because she can make a deeper incision, and great fear is at hand. And if necessity calls for it, so it is fitting that you request a midwife well-versed in this art, and take care not to be present when one, and if you do not find her, then seek out the subtlest of midwives; and the present a wise bailiff in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands that she make what you command from the inquiry of the thigh; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: so it is fitting to give her a pill or foundation and seek out the thigh; and if she finds it, then she constrains it in its place, and commands him to put a pill into her mouth with the patient, and wants and presses his left hand on the bladder form.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If it has come to be true, it is fitting that she move from one place to another with great care from the entrance of the bladder up to below the groin, until she comes to the root of the thigh; then strike above the stone in the root of the thigh towards the middle, where it feels like a nail, and does not feel anything above or below the stone, and tie off the first tendon; then pour the liquor into the tendon, if you feel the stone is very close to the wound so that it can come out for sure, and see that there are many kinds of stones: this is to know, namely small ones, big ones, hard ones, soft ones, long ones, round ones, and those with rust.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you see the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if they do not boast, put vitriol on the affected area and let it burn for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the stone comes out, and you have the discharges that I told you about when extracting stones from the abdomen, in order to assist you with your work. And if they do not boast, and this is of the artery which has been cut off, put powder on the wound and the strained tendon and bended skin, and do not resume the treatment again, lest the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is eased and the pus is drained, so that it stops coming out, then your work is finished until the opening is made.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshed hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rice water is nothing but a mixture of moisture or white pus, which is under the skin, beneath the joint, where the blood collects; and it is called "syfac", and it's never truly in the linen of the blood, if one thinks it's another wound; and that's the leather of the vein between the white syfac that we have said; and this happens neither by chance nor design.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rice water is from weakness that comes into the joints, and spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes if it comes from a blow on the bones, and this moisture has many colors: or the color is declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or white, and more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, because if it is like white as we have said, then there are abscesses returning, I saw so long that the figures resemble an ox, and they do not open up the bones, because they have moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the skin, then the abscesses return with a part of the muscle, and because of this, people think it resembles another ox; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white part, if one smells well; therefore, when you see that you know the color of the moisture, examine the entire interior of the quadrangular space, because the form is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to those who come after the intercessory person, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat him with iron, it is fitting that the patient be healthy according to our skill and the replenishment of his body; then take care on his back, above one thing a little high, and wrap over him much linen; then sit above his left side, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two bones near the joints; then take the spatulum with wine, and cut the skin of the joints from the long joint up to the nail, making a straight cut in dividing the skin of the joints just as white as snow, and burn it subtly according to our skill; then pierce the joint plain with water at I large puncture, and extract all the water, and then put on your linen, and set the joint together; and do not touch the skin of the joints, but only the joint itself; cut them all equally or otherwise, so that you will not make it badly, for if you do not, he will return to his wound; and if his blood should flow to your hand, then straighten him in his place when you have completed the work on the joint; then assemble the two joints of the near bones at one costure, then cure him as with other wounds, until he is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the corrupted flesh of another disease, then it is fitting that you tie up the vessels that are suspended in doubt about the decrement of blood; then strike the clot at all the suspended area, and extract the flesh, and cure as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if an inflammation is assembled in two parts together, which you know are two branches; then strike the other part as you have done the first equally, then apply ointment to the blood, and place a moist linen cloth on the wound; put over it another moist linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and cover with two plaits of double cloths, and fasten it all up according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the two cloths, and use woolen stuff according to this shape and assemble them by sewing in the collar of the braies; and one of the knuckles presses on the foundation just up to the back, and the others at the side of the elbow; and the other two above the two angles, and so all the rest is assembled the tightened belt in the sleeve of the braie; and this branch can be treated with cautery in place of iron cutting, when you take a subtle cauterizing knife, and strike the skin around the veins, so that the white mass contained in the pus is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this shape, and pierce it on the vein, and scorch with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	Instruct the patient to try all methods until you are sure; and guard that fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is safer; and take care of preventing the flow of blood, and watch out for the damage caused by cutting or opening wounds; and if nothing goes against what has been said about apotemesis, open the chest or cut out any tumors or other things, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is fearful and will not follow this work because of its horror, perforate, as I have told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs which we have said should be applied to water, if you fix the patient on a high seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with a wide instrument; and make the perforation deep into the body; and let the pus flow out widely; then put cotton over the wound, tie it up, and leave for the remaining blood to drain off; then treat the wound until it is healed; and if the blanched cloth does not allow the blood to come out of the mouth of the wound, it is advisable that you poke or with the instrument used to treat the dropsy, because the shape is as before mentioned; and enlarge the wound, and know when the blood returns and is assembled after six months or in what time is passed, and when it has become assembled, as before, and thus will pass the patient's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	It is known that in the removal of this type of limb there are many deaths and painful dispositions, therefore I think it should be left; and I will tell you about the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that most abscesses occur on the body, and in itself as a limb, and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is because of superfluity of sour and acidic blood which spreads to the joints, or from percussion; and its colour according to the colour of the body; for it causes no pain, but is a painful abscess; and sometimes it is a grievous and painful abscess, with a fleshy color, and never comes from another artery, or swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it's from another artery, so is diagnosed by the shape of the abscess when you press it with your two fingers; and do not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are swollen with blood are diagnosed by their shape at the point of touch on the two fingers, and can be easily recognized as a lump, and similarly as other swellings; and to cut the exact place of the vein, then lift it up high, and pull out the surrounding substance from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already swollen with these swellings, then it is necessary that you treat the vein and cut it; and if it's swollen in the sac, or inside the vessels, then it's necessary to deliver all of that space, and cut it round.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the child is near you, so it is fitting that you copy it whole, and extract the afterbirth, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound of soft woolen cloth in olive oil and wine, then give the cure of other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the tonsils.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has been enveloped with an enveloping tissue like the boar, with the swelling of the tonsils, and the patients die greatly when it comes; and the cure for this disease is well-prone just as previously stated, and we will tell you of its work according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to sit on the elevated bed, then pour the bitters into his mouth down towards the throat, at all the vessels near by, and stretch out the master veins, and extend them; then cut in the spatumile so that it cuts through the bones, as far as they are exposed, and then scrape from each part, just as we have said in extracting the arteries which are in the temples; then put a needle where there is an artery, and tie it to the first vein where it came out, and tie it behind the other head; then cut straight up, according to the length of the body, and take away the corrupted vessels; then cure the wound just as we have said for those who are pierced by arrow, so that none of the vessels come from harm, and since all the vessels seem healthy again, it is necessary to tie the vessels at all the places.
de la routure dou syfac	Of surgical incision of the nose
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The dangers of this type of surgery arise from the section that comes out of the nose, or from stretching on the abdomen in the area of the angers, because the intestine descends from that incision to one of the joints; and this incision is either at the nose or by stretching, and these two kinds of causes come: either by percussion, or by falling, or by burning, or by lifting a pain-filled grief, and by similar things; and the signs when there is a spreading of the nasal section are that it comes out little by little over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal until near the end, because the nose presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the nose that brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear different under the skin, below the skin, and it's because of the intestine coming out and the body voiding of the nose.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it is done with the corks (or intestines) and retained in that place, causing great suffering to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And for these iron treatments with fear, because it is necessary to flee from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way to treat this injury is that you command the patient to put the intestine into the wound if it can fit inside; then take a piece of string between your fingers and tie above the neck. Lift up the shoulders; then stab the wound from top to bottom, cutting all the skin around the joints until you have four fingers' length. Then close the wound with two strands of that string, so that no thread can enter in or any vein comes out; and put a knot on top of the first one, two inches long, and after that, the other according to the circumference of the joint; then cut at the place under the skin around the joints, just as we said before; then put linen soaked in oil into the wound, and tie it with that same string.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes cauterize the white flesh after we have said so, by incision, out of doubt about the slowing down of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this has happened many times, and let the binding be so that it will stick to him; and if it lingers at the wound, whether it is from hot water, and apply what we have said, until it sticks; then treat the wound with another cure, until he is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a hairy groin
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done just as the splinter is gathered from the flesh, in this manner: you tie the straps, after the waist, lightly above and below; then chop with an arrow, and treat the abscess that works, until the straps ache; and cure as we have said, until he is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you hit the hairs, if it bleeds and cures the wound, so that it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ligature is tight, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is more moist in this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin around the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	It often softens the skin of the joints in some people, because those who are inside are softened, and it's easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and strikes the soft skin above the natural skin; then assemble the two leaves against a suturing, and if you see, cut through the first three layers or four firmly; then strike between the layers, and the cure like other wounds, until he is healed, and the hair falls.
dou chastrement	a cautery of fire
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Knows that cautery is in our law, and it pleases me not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two ways: one is that the physicians know how to respond when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we have often had need of cauterization of some animals to help us, just as of oxen and sheep and goat and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we do by attraction, we sit the patient best in hot water, until their flesh is softened and relaxed; then we press them with our hands, until they are removed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The patient must be tied with the best string and press the skin of the groin with your left hand, then suspend the string and strike each limb at one stroke, when you have well scraped them; and let no point of the sting remain on the flesh and the subtle stinging that is over the vestments; and this method of chastenment is more gentle than the one made by attraction, because the attraction remains by chance some things of the skin, because of which the best desires excess; then cure the wound until it is sane.
des hermofrodites	For those with hemi-fallicosis (hermaphroditism)
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	The hermaphrodit is according to two manners of being at home: one is that the two groin areas are open like the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes in his crotch there is urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and has on its finger like a thorn and two knots.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for fever and hunger is that you copy the tied signs all together, and treat it as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine comes out through their perineum skin, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the ingrown toenail
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The ingrown toenail is a tied sign on the natural part, so long as it's too ugly to see; and some women have it just as large as their thumb, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to dye the inflammation of the ingrown toenail on your hand or near the nail, and do it lightly; and don't go too deep, lest there be bleeding, then the treatment for other treatments until it's healed; and another sign that appears at the mouth of the mucus, and the tongue, and sometimes it bursts forth, and is like a cow, and for this they called it the old "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is fitting that you copy it, just as we have said, and perform the treatment until she is healed.
de erratique	of fault or carelessness
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Error is when the nature of a woman is not perceived, or the fault is sought in her; it is caused by nature at birth, or by accident through illness that has come upon her, or it is due to injury from a blow, or the sin of giving birth with difficulty or pain, and it is created by its own force in the uterus, in the groin, or under, or whatever way; and they are not able to conceive, and childbirth, and by chance, flowers may appear; and knowledge of this is acquired through experience, from gazing at the appearance of a newborn.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is near to appearing, then choose to your right or left.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is swollen from the surgery, and it is near two fingers, then go to it quickly, and do as follows: put your two index fingers together, and the woman lies on her back, spread out her legs; then set the two fingers in formation, until the swelling of the incision subsides, and the stitches come loose; then take linen, and ghee (oil) with wool, and apply it to the wound, and have the woman lie down at home every day, so that she cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the incision is hard and thick, it is advisable to cut with a spatula similar to leaves of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stitches are of charnel ( probably a reference to animal sinew or cordage) and it adheres to the bone, cut with caution and apply; and have the medicines that stain blood, like saffron, dragon's blood, incense, and an abundance of olive oil; then bring in a large wooden spoon if the wound cannot heal; and do this for a long time, and bring in a linen tent dry; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the marrow comes out through a new scar, if they wish to cover it according to this manner, unless it is an abscess enchantress.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	But when the abscess has formed in the marrow, one should not touch fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually occur, and when old hemorrhoids form they become swellings; and we have said in the division about the signs and symptoms, I will say here which ones can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and swellings when they are filled with marrow and do not feel, unless it is cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh can be felt, so they can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then bind the ankle with tongs, and cut at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as vinegar and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour her feet into boiling water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she bleeds, take her to sit in a decoction of sumac and grape pomace and gales and similar things, and then mix flour with honey and easy, and make it impregnate on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If they don't do it with fire cautery, instruct the patient to make hot vents on their back and strike at the breasts; then take linen, and the pus in the juice of plantain or in the juice of agrimony with wine, and make them breathe.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess repose, cure the patient with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a head like a horse's head, so they should cover as I have said; and then cure the patient until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of swellings from the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marrow, such as canker and bone abscesses and herpes and eczema and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Instruct the patient to let it rest for a while until the pain is gone; and then have the patient sit on two stools or so that they lean, and support their back and assemble their legs according to what is necessary in front of the leg; and stretch out their knees, and put their arms below their knees, and bind them well with a good tie; then draw the needle towards the right side, and bring it into the passage where one works the mouth of the molar, so that after this comes the form; and it is fitting that when you see the instrument brought into this passage, that you put the point first by knowing the depth of the molar, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and do not harm the patient; and if the instruments are large, so as to cover the depth of the molar with cloths, so that the instruments do not grieve the patient; and it is fitting that he puts the corner of the instrument on top, and tightens the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the marrow, then it is advisable to avoid using iron, but treat it as we have said when dividing.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The first thing of skill is to know the figure of natural childbirth, and when you see the woman go into labor, and desire to push out the afterbirth, then hasten the birth of the child quickly; for in that case you will know whether it is a natural delivery, with the issue coming out under its head, and the second parting with it; and when you see these signs, it is advisable to press lightly on her abdomen, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it pushes up its head, then the second parting comes with it, and the marrow of its excesses is cleansed by proper purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it often happens with its feet and limbs, and comes upon the chest or the head, and sometimes comes over the belly, or somewhere else, and is changed by chance before its neck, and other bad figures; so it is necessary to the physician that they be skillful and subtle in these things, and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the ways how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon his head by natural cause, and the pregnant woman cries out in pain, and the virtues of it are weak, then let him sit on a stool, or the women hold him; and since its nature is oil or fenugreek, let him drink the bile between his two thumbs with the small spatula that has this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And slice the second limb, and strike at his joint until the moistures that are in the fire are exhausted; and put back to life the woman's belly as long as the fever does not descend; and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to bind the woman with muskilaige of fenugreek with oil of silex; then let him eat and vomit with condissi, and hold his mouth and nose for an hour: thus now the fever.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is fitting that you let them come in little by little; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on the bed, and lift her feet high; then turn the bed over towards the ground, and hold the woman, so she does not catch a fall while being turned; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife that is placed before, and extract the child, and let them come in evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the limbs of the child on their feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on its feet, it is fitting to push them up high; and then turn them little by little, until they are even; then grab their feet and extend them a little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he wants to jump just as quickly, so the command has him prick, and the blood is made to flow from his condition; if he jumps then God heals.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not so as we have said, if the wound heals little by little, until it follows the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For this is a good thing.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come about as we have said, so he takes muscillaige from alum, and oil of simeon, and gumboose melted, and grinds everything in mortar; and applies the nature of a woman's body inside and avoids this ointment, then makes him sit in vinegar until under the ribs; and when it is softened under, he makes the collier of mirrour, and puts it on, and lets him go lightly, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the issue of a child from his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it meets with its feet so little by little; then put the belly on its back, and let the feet go down, and be placed on an elevated bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then press the hands up to the wind, and uncover the crotch below, until she is dressed below; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and fix them in place, then put the belly upwards again, then strike at the hands; and let the child come down little by little; and instruct the woman to bind herself so that the child takes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	Of a child coming out with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I therefore advise bringing back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, if she gets up and walks; if she cannot walk, I lay her on the bed and straighten out her legs; then apply the poultice that I have mentioned; and if she does not conceive, I make her sit on the stool, then study bringing back the hand; and let the child be brought to its natural figure, and let it bring forth, and instruct her to bind herself until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	After the child is born, it has a mark on its neck and its hands are spread out and its face turned towards its back, mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I advise that the baby has a mark on its hand, then it is turned little by little, and slightly set free; and when it is even, it applies muslard oil to its back and olive oil, as we have said, then commands it to move a little; and when you have done this, place it in a chair, and commands it to grip; and let it be released.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner as the rest of this line
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this manner to the rest of these lines, cut the vein at one spot until the moisture is dry; and if the child spits on its face and neck, cut from the root, so that it is not held back, and the child dies; then pour the child into a container, as far as you have put it, and command the woman to grip herself never again: afterwards, let it be released lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born many times, and sometimes no ones at all or three; and this is not a strange thing, for it has rarely happened.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live if they have no name; I know that they are multiplied and brought forth by the seed which divides them, which is linked to the womb; and sometimes they are born just as naturally as we all are, just as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born with strength, then the cure is as we have said, and let them be handled gently, and take effect quickly and lightly what it does; and do so just as the fruit ripens for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
