Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if his breasts become swollen after many days, he knows that his breast is not well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the subtle veins are cut after a long time, do not despair of your health, for your health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who delay for a long time in healing from the heat of the fire in their wounds, and from those that do the opposite; and if his breast becomes swollen after many days, he knows that his breast is not well; and if his breast takes a long time to heal, and is far away, then apply moist substances to the substance and dry virtues, as oil dissolves, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is a later medicine; take ointment definit, and mix it with rose oil, and white vinegar equal in proportion; then confine and use. The same thing makes cooked honey to swell up when the ointment definit is not present; or take mirrors and aloes and incense, and grind them, and make powder on the honey when it's heated over the fire; and then wrap it around the breast, and never administer an Aristogeiton long, nor roots of celestial lily, which is like flour of violets and centaury; and use either simple or composite remedies: grind them, and make a powder, and mix with the honey I said before, and apply it; and if the cure is prolonged, and does not heal by this cure, then know that corruption has entered in full, and made impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on joints.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the elephant
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A swelling that occurs under the elephant's hide near the arm or foot, or sometimes in other places; and when it is old and not taken care of, if they open it up and cut at it, they will run and jump and move about until they reach the root of the ulcer, and perhaps they will get to its very center; and the corrosions come just beneath the bone, so that there is great pain, and the swelling is large and red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then it is necessary to copy over the entire remaining inflammation of the ulcer, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the joint is healthy; and if the joint presses on the flesh, and begins to pierce, and the wound, so it is wise to put the right under the joint so that it points the flesh, and the bale in its top, and strike that flesh subtly and lightly, and set upon the remainder of the flesh medicines hot and corrosive to remove all; then the cure of pain shall be long as it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, if you strike and pull it out, because as long as the bone is corrupted it cannot heal; and if you see it corrupting on the other side, strike at its root so as it has been said, then cure until it heals; and if it is ironed and baled, and it feels great pain, it is wise to first cure it before striking the joint with a small spanner in cutting across from above, and take care that the cut does not come near the flesh under the joint, because the patient will feel too much pain; and if it has corrupted, then place something on top which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain comes from the ear.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints which are injured in the hands of some men by chance may be broken, and sometimes there is a break or an injury to the bones, and never a sprain; and it never happens that they give birth to any joint at the root of the joint, or that the birth occurs in any of the joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that are born without any sound or movement in the two joints may not move at all, and those that are born with a joint may sometimes not move; the weight of the person who is broken so much is lighter, in this manner: he weighs less in his root of a large spatumile.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those born at the root of a joint are crippled to cure: if they have a covering.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the newborn or those about to be born out of water, if it is deemed necessary, first copy around the circumference of the bone just beneath the bone, then cut the bone at a suitable length for that person, and treat them until they are healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The patient who comes to be treated for some disturbance in the assembly of their body comes by birth, or through sudden injury, or from being burned with fire, or through similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is deemed necessary to close the wound, so that they can be repaired according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or drapes moistened in olive oil, so that they do not stick together; or put between two subtle pieces of cloth, until they are closed, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the wound comes to be in either of its two parts with the palm, then close it as is fitting.
des vils	Old viles
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The big veins that are swollen and filled with a melancholy fluid come out in many more limbs of the body; and it happens more often to those who go barefoot and walk and work, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, it is necessary that you do not administer any purgation of gallstone, but rather the salve of the basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron remedy is done in two ways: one is to cut them and apply the black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting remedy is done in this way: first raise the leg of water very hot, until the great vein is exposed and subtle, then strain the leg of the sick from above down to the knee; then cut the vein in three places, a large one, then elevate and drain the black blood by hand, from head to toe, as long as the patient can bear it; and then tie, and command that they abstain from meat with black gall; and repeat the evacuation and treatment whenever the veins are full, and bring harm to the sick.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s'il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d'aigue chaude tant qu'elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n'as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the arm is bent and twisted and turned together, and it is not straight, as we have said, so it must be cut sharply, but not covered up; and taken out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron used to cut the arm when it is curved, and not sharpened, will spoil the vein; for if it were a fine curve, we would pierce the vein, but since it is a large one, as we have said, you should do this.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is tied off in the legs, in warm areas where there are no herbs or trees growing, and on dry earth where there is no moisture; and it may occur in other places besides the legs, and this happens because of putrefaction that comes from below the skin, for just as a snake comes inside the body through the skin, so too does putrefaction come out.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein opening indicate that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then change the blood, and as soon as it begins to flow out, just like the sap of an oak tree.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the joint opens, it is advisable to wrap a piece of linen around one and a half fingers length along the joint up to two and a half, the nail, and leave the linen on the leg, and at all times that it is not exposed, if you wrap the linen around the nail; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, and do not cover its root, until it is entirely empty; for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh, and bring with it abscesses and putrefaction or decay, and bad malady; therefore this thing should be treated little by little until the chief, and there remains nothing in the body; and I have seen once that this vein opened up to two palms of length, or ten, and one hour ago, a man came to me whose vein opened up from ten palms of length, and when you cut it, you poured out one pint or less, and the point was at its source, so that everything emptied; and there is no remaining matter inside, and you should administer medicines to heal any decay for each day, then the cure should be done as usual with the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bursts, and even when she opens in the joint of the foot or the toe, and it comes out a great amount of blood, and it springs forth; therefore cure her then as we have told before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that hatch between leather and skin
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "bovine disease", because it often affects cattle, and it has small worms that hatch between the skin and leather, and they move all over the body, going up and down, and causing great pain to every part, until the skin splits or they emerge, and then they burst forth; and it is infected with foul pus from some humors, such as serpents, lice, and worms, and one doubts its malice because when it moves through the body, it goes up to the head, and sometimes comes out at the eye, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see someone being cured and treated, if the fever does not subside until it passes: then it is necessary that you hold the patient above and below with a strong bond tightly, then strike on top and treat him, and if the abscess bursts from within in the chest, and you do not find it, then cauterize the wound with fire until he dies; and the greatest harm it causes, as we have said, is that they are poisoned by oil, just like we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the head near the oil, tighten below the eyelid firmly, then strike on top, and treat him; and it is necessary to use the patient with the medicine of purgative body for the bad humors that are polluted, and war with spoiled food and rotten meat.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This sickness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, moving from member to member; and I have seen this what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of one of her arms; and soon afterwards, I saw it rising as if like a worm at the shoulder, even sooner than anything else, as quickly as living silver when cutting through her to another; the pain departed from that place, and lodged itself in the shoulder, and then a little later ran all along the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she was turning again around the body, just like I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed much how she moved about from member to member, because I had never seen this sickness in that manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I have seen many that have wanted to move their pain elsewhere, but I do not want it myself, just as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was for this reason that the woman has a stiff body, and covered breasts, and appears with these constrained movements; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are robust, and have moist bodies and women's skin.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when I see how to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens itself like we said, apply the plaster on both sides and in haste, then strike above so that the constrained movements cease in the limb; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see with your eyes, then the cure of one who tightens the veins, such as fetid pills, serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	The extraction of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the state of the body or where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their points is that there are those with great points and small ones, and those with arrows, and those with angled heads, and those with tips, and of those where there are pieces; and the one which pierces in any member pierces according to two manners: either in a principal member piercing, such as brain, liver, stomach, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it then pierces in any of those members and the signs of death appear, which I will tell you later, it is necessary to be cautious that you remove this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions; and when no sign appears, and the arrow does not penetrate deeply, you should throw away the wound and cure the injury.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l'os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d'entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t'aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s'elle n'est ens.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the vein when it bleeds or blood is drawn out, is that it is near the left groin and feels as if it had been struck by a hard object, not hollow; and by chance the vein stops like the feet, and comes with black sweat and cold fever, and fainting; notice then that this has a sign of death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not bring pain is when it emerges from the wound without any bloody discharge, and the throat swells, and the patient becomes pale, and breathes deeply, and sighs with great fear.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow goes into the covering of the belly, so that it lodges between the small ribs; and it brings forth great pain and great suffering, and the patient breathes deeply; and all the limbs on both sides become numb.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow goes into the stomach, by chance it comes out of the wound without anything from undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow goes into the belly, and it comes out of the wound without any discharge at all by the bowels' route, then there is no hope for recovery or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If an arrow is shot into him while he has an open wound, and the blood flows out from it, and the urine flows out quickly and comes forth in a stream, and the patient feels great pain; know that the injury is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arm and the shoulder and the throat and the elbow and the axillary region and the spine on his back and the muscles and the chest and the legs, and the limb resembling them, are saved according to the various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because of this that you may do similarly.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened in my house with an arrow stuck in the neck or arm, at the base of the neck: I tried to pull it out, and pulled from the other side below the fat of the ear, and was made whole without any discomfort.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	Instruct the patient to tie an arrow onto the fatty tissue under the skin with a paper strip underneath, and when the strip is returned, only grasp the tip towards the fist, and it was an arrow as long as a Turkish bow, all of iron lighter than an ear; the game was safe, and no other bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And tie an arrow onto the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow in the ear: I shaved the beards, and made it as subtle as I could, so that when I tied it, the Christian was safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And tie an arrow onto a man in the house who was down with fever or wind, and I thought he was dying; but then he passed XXX days without any improvement; so I cut up the bowstring, and tied it again, and there was no other bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you visit a man who has an arrow stuck in his back or on his side, and the wound is closed over, and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural disposition, nor finds any discomfort in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And visit another man who has an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound is closed over; and he suffers greatly for a long time and many other pains.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And another arrow was stuck in the man who is king of the princes, and it was stuck in his nose, and he was leaning to the right side; and the arrow was fully inserted. I was summoned to the doctor after that for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I will translate it for you:
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I put above the stomach implant, digestive tract, because the liver swells; and appeared to me the livers of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I had put the implant in my hand days ago, and resolved the wound directly, and kept the patient long until he felt his side hurt from within; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put medicine with corrosive properties on the wound by hand for days, until it was open, and tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which dried out in the liver; then I adjusted in the opening of the wound with that medicine, so that the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and passed well through the ends for four months, and then burst out if I did not cut with tongs, one from this side and the other, and could not come out; therefore I didn’t cease to subtlety and invent methods with instruments, until I took it one day with tongs well made, according to what came in the end of this chapter, so that I would try and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The doctor judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I will restore it anyway, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me the quality of extracting any arrow wounds, so that you put your cure on what I did not say, for the books cannot know everything; but the wise masters have knowledge of a little thing, and know well what is present and failing, find new work and nine instruments, to remove the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows wound the limbs or they are inserted in two manners: either by the joint where they enter, or by another part; and the one which is shot into him now will always be an arrow that enters his flesh.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Et s'elle ne saut maintenant, so let her lie until the flesh is rotting and she is covered in pus; and also if she is stuck into the bone and cannot get out, so let her lie for some days, and move every day; and thus she will burst, and if she does not burst, then pierce within to find out whether all the pus has been removed, until the swelling subsides, and then take her out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If an arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and begins to move towards one of the wounds of the brain, and any of the events I have mentioned regarding the patient: if you do not treat it, but let her lie until she becomes equal after some days, for if the arrow comes into that very space, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck in the bone alone, and does not come out there for a while, and the patient remains some days without another accident, then it is advisable to use the method of traction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck in such a way and cannot come out for long, then take tares (possibly referring to the use of tare or another herb) around it, as I have said; then treat the patient until they are healthy again.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to the body in someone's dwelling if it cannot be seen, and the person has no way to remove it; and if you feel it, if there is a suitable instrument for it; and if you cannot compress the wound or see through the depth of the arrowhead, and there is no bone or nerve visible, then pull out as much of the arrow as you can; and if you can do so, and if the arrow has ear-shaped parts where it holds, break off or bend the ears of the arrow until you can remove them; and be careful not to break the arrow, but rather extract it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, so that the pain reaches until your joints are torn apart, then take away the extraction, because the extraction is a lie.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if they come back with blood against the treatment you are doing, then apply what we have said in that chapter; and be careful of the incision on the nerve and vein, and put in (the following) method so that you can treat the arrow as soon as it is cut off, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to how he was when the arrow cut him, because this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot do it, then put him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, if it is opening something, or if the skin is inflamed in one place, whether you see it or feel it somewhere: take then a higher size, until the tongs can reach, and then pull it out: if there's a chance now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, turn your hand around it, so that she goes into the bone, and opens up the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If she cannot come out, let her alone again, and then continue the extraction until she comes out; and if there is an arrow stuck in it, pour medicine all over the entire arrow; and if it has been cast away, and you see that it needs treatment, administer a headband instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then pour, and if the arrow is caught, pour the instrument with a point entering in, to relieve the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is touched off, it is suitable to copy the entire length of the shaft or where the venom is, if you can; then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	In case of an arrow shot into the belly, near the spleen, or in the bladder, or on the side, and it is close, you can cover over it, if it has pierced; and protect the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then cauterize the wound, if necessary, as is proper; and the cure until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium-sized, and small ones, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the forceps with a hooked nail is similar to the feather of a bird, in order to push against the tip of the arrow, as it looks like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pressing and holding if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Veins that bring healing are XXXI, because there is XVI, namely: two branches behind the ears, called "the two herbs"; and two arteries in the two temples appearing; and two veins in the two temple corners, called "aspirers"; and a vein at the forehead; and a vein at the top of the nose; and the two tendons on the neck; and the two veins above the lips, which are called "augeriches"; and the two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that bring healing are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is located on the left side of the chest, and they call it "the vein of the head" among the common people; and the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic is located on the right side of the chest, and they call it "the vein of the abdomen", and it is located above the diaphragm, and that one brings healing, which opens up clearly under the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The saved vein is the one between the earlobe and the little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the first is below the wing of the shoulder on the left side, where the vein is sewn to the bone of the left side; and the second branch is at the ankle on the right side; and the third vein called "nesse" is at the heel of the other side.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins that are behind the ears help with old catharses and emigration, and its quality is as I tell you, and it is that you lift the patient's head, and rub the vein or the veins on a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with one pin, until both veins appear behind the ears in two places of the head: if those do not happen, and you feel the pulse below them, sign that you must incise; then take the lancet, and push it through under the vein next to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, cut and the skin and the vein well two should go through, and make come out of the wound until you see; then bind and tie, until she is healed; and I have said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Instruct the patient that if you have an ulcer on the temple, and a sore, and eye inflammation accustomed, and water in the eyes with the eyelids; then you should tie the wrists so they do not move until the blood has come out. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein in front is worth as much as the sickness of the head as old diseases of the face, and of emigration, and of redness; and the qualities are such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "scaffer", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And set the point on the vein, and press above with your hand, or with another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then release the patient’s neck, and tie the vein until it is clean and never again bleeding excessively.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	But it is not advisable to cut the veins too deeply; and the vein cutting across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the vein when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The patient should bind the two veins that are in two layers when they bleed at the arm, and the tunic, and the rosy cheeks, and the eyebrow in oil, and with maladies of the face; and the qualities of their sickness are such that the patient turns his neck on twisting any thread, just like before. Then he heals, and if the healing is through a wound, a little long in the flame, a little wide, for there is no part of him that has character.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break; then make a stitch of the wound, as much as you need it, and then tie above the cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The wound of the neck with new flesh is valuable for ague, and for sores that are far-fetched, and for maladies of the face, such as inflammation and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the wound are such that the patient twists his neck, then twists his neck to your left hand, and takes a subtle flame long, and puts it on the eyebrow between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in this place, and the pain will begin now to come. Do not go too far up, and make a stitch of the wound as much as you need it, then tie it for one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to tighten the vein, and at the beginning of surgery, and in a great many diseases, and emphysema, and corruption, and herpes, and ulcers; and the qualities of the disease are such that the patient strains his neck away from one side and the other, as we have said; and let the master stand above the chief of the sick, and the sick person sit on the second stool, then tie the vein tightly for a long time, tempering with blood, or until it is necessary; then do the same thing in the other vein, then cut the ligature, and tighten and loosen the veins slightly, so that the patient does not choke; and let him stay just until morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	About the disease of the thighs.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The patient from the wounded veins of the lips above so that they can assist with coal in the mouth, and corruption of gums, fissures of lips, and do not eat nor drink.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the wound if are to have him sit before you, and strain his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by that they are black, and because they have thinner, black veins: strike then one and the other, and if you do not know which is which, and you are in doubt, then strike the biggest of each part, and do it to both the upper and lower veins, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the wound below the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The patient who has a vein below the tongue is aided after the head injury, and it's at the tightening of the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and with diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of healing are such that the patients will be between your hands in front of the sun, and lift the tongue, and look down on each side one vein black: then heal both one and the other, and do not go too far by cutting, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the elbow are cut according to two manners: either by piercing at the entire width of the mitten-like vein, or with olive oil subtle as one cuts with scissors, and it's called "anestil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of mercury is very famous, and it is large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And is used to open the vein-filled arteries with flat, rough skin of great blood and pus; and it is the form of the flame olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle in point, and is used to save the fine veins, or it has subtle citron blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, greatly aids in the treatment of diseases below the neck, and on the throat, and on the belly, and on the abdomen; and it is necessary for the doctor that he cures quickly, and warms himself with the artery that is under.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes out, then he must stop bleeding, as I have said; and it should not be pinched with the flame, but rather cut like honey.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	In case the basilic vein does not open up clearly, it is advisable to extract it and replace it with another one, or if you want rain of blood, or if you keep the wounded person in their bed: it opens up clearly; and strike at the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the vein of the wound, it is also advisable to extract the arm so that you can feel the pulse; then mark the vein and tie the arm, and strike at the wound with a fiery blade; beware that you do not cut into the artery when you see the vein inflamed, for this is an artery: exclude therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see that it is bulging up high as the urine of a child, and it is not red and subtle, take note that it is not an artery: hasten then, and put your two fingers on long; then pull out your finger if they are bloody, because this has happened many times; tie the arm, and let it remain in that state, and do not move the afflicted person; and be cautious, and do not move them until they recover.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If they are not cauterized and he comes, and the medicine is not present, then strike the artery if it opens up, because the head of the joint retreats; and lance him.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a scab of fistula and cut it, and take one of the halves and tie well to the other half; if he is not cauterized, this is good; if not, then the cure will do so as we have said, with the powders that cauterize blood; and the cauterizations are not good in more severe conditions because of the small size of the wound, and for the power of the ligature on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The sickness of the vein in the middle so far is that it treats blood on the head above, and beneath the body, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it is fitting for the lord that he warms himself for the nerve which is below, and if he punctures too much towards the bone, and wounds the nerve, and swells, and cures are bad, and by chance cannot cure; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person because of its subtlety, then you should take out the healthy sains from the instrument anesil; and cut the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if they have blood between the two nerves, apply pressure to the long part.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The remedy for the headache is to apply blood to the head, and aid the eyes; and it is advisable to puncture with olive oil or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all bloods, since it does not disturb the nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In any case, it is advisable to seek the lighter remedy first, and do not trouble anything if you need it for the first time, and repeat it; and by chance, some swellings occur in men that one needs to experience for the first time, but it will cause no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first line is:
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick who are being treated have no fixed hour or time for illness, but when the need is of day or night, in all hours and at all times; and it does not suit to heal children before they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus more than six months before birth.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And it does not suit to heal the elderly who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And if someone wishes to be healed in any manner, then it is fitting that they should have the intestines cleansed of a light purgative, if they have a great amount of gallstones retained, so that the veins do not burst with excessive flow into the intestines and cause harm to the principal members; nor does one heal who is excessively fat, or who is feverish, whatever the cause may be, or dropsical; and if someone becomes sick after suffering from colic, vomiting, and inflammation of the abdomen, and frequent urination, and heavy work, watching, and labor, then subtlely treat the humors, removing the excess without being too fat, by food and drinks and medicines, taking advantage of the opportunity; then take a bath, if any condition prevents it, in order to subtly treat the sickness, and heal from the side into the third position, as we have said; and be careful on the day of work, pain, luxury, and similar things; and may you remain bound and joyful, and may your sainieres (healers) be higher than those who are healed, and may they rub the arms two or three times, then extract the bandage from above in a moderate manner, because when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot be corrected without; and then rub them with clean hands until the veins swell and feel on; then anoint the sainieres with the flame of a little old oil, then put some amount of their own left hand's thumb on that vein below the elbow, whenever they wish to heal, so that the vein does not burst and fail to be pierced by the needle.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For in those veins that flow like cords in the vein, and for those that are full of windiness, when you put a flame on them, they retract back to the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is that; and if they cover the vein, then the wound is too narrow, so it is fitting for the surgeons to be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, it is good; but if not, then reapply some of that fluid under or above it, as quickly as possible, so that the veins are swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen and the patient expects to die, if he allows himself one day or two, and does not tie up his arm: by chance there may come an abscess; or do not enter the bath, then reapply the surgery whenever it pleases; and if the opening is small, or if you see a lot of blood, so that you fear it will not occur again, be bold in the same opening with all the flame directly; and open it quickly, so that the veins are swollen; for this has happened many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelled limb, do not resume the treatment again, and apply a little bit of lard oil, because it lightens the body with pain, and is muddied in this limb the same lard that is oil; and so minister the lard oil to each wound that you treat, to dry out the flow of pain; and the same thing does triacle and bowel of horse, when one puts it on the limb; so subtlety is lost and splintered when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If it comes to a large abscess, which has often happened, and it is only treated at those times when the opening of the vein is small, you hasten, and apply a moist sponge soaked in water and wine, and wrap it around the limb tightly for an hour; it is likely that you will do this after the issue of the pain from the vein, and if it remains on the limb after some days without any injury or harm, it will not hurt; and if you see, apply some aloes or mirror mixed with juice of calendane, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times occurs an abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica: put then your hand up, and if you find the joint swollen at the pressure of the hand, that is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put on any of those things which we have said, because in haste without the artery; but make it dry and cool to harden the joint, and then apply another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if it is not black, let it escape until it turns red; and if you see it is thick, let it escape until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	Instruct the patient who is weak and feeble, and has need for bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and apply larger fizzes; and to the weak person do the opposite, and it is better to heal quickly and often, and one should heal him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is safe from deterioration of blood and from bruising of nerves, and is worth more than the long healing through the thin or the large.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose blood needs the healing, it is recommended to give him milky pain moist in pomegranate juice; if he is warm, he should be cut with a bloodletting three times or four times; and if he has a cold complexion, make his pain moist beforehand in rose syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	Instruct the patient to let his palm be injured, after a large amount of blood has been drawn, if it is deemed necessary that he drink a warm broth of char, and an odorant sweet syrup, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.

If he wants to heal one arm and another time, if it is deemed necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, then let him recover little by little, according to the amount of his continued virtue.

Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be healed on the other side, if he should need to be healed on the second or third day.

Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, and fait venir fievre; 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is escaped, so let it be left and do not hold it tight, until the abscess is allayed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If you need to treat the wound for a second time, do so with the same vein as the one in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is sutured in place of the vein on the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of suturing is that the patient pours his hand into hot water, until the wound is red; then tie it loosely, so that the vein appears well; and now sew across, not too long or too short; and if there are large gaps, suture them well near the joint of the hand, and if they cannot come out, put the hand back in hot water, and let the wound run in the water until you have enough; and if it's so good, do not pour the hand again into hot water, for it is put more into winter than into summer; and sutureting from this vein is more saved from all other veins, as there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Injury of the left hand is worth all kinds of diseases of the liver; and this is the way: strain the hand, and pour in hot water, until the wound be clean, if you see; and if it's injured across, and if you hit it all over, so that nothing grieves; and don't walk too much on it by force, because the nerves are dried out of use at that time, and then put the hand back in hot water, if they are not frozen in the wound, and do not come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have cut the wound as much as is necessary to it, put some oil and sinew on the vein to bind it up hastily, and do this for each cut.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Injury of the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse; and do it in the same way as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickle of the spleen is worth all kinds of diseases that are outside the body, such as illnesses of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the bowels, and the joints, and the legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his spleen are such that if sick men put some stone in hot water and rub upon the vein till it dies, and lie on top of the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, then they go out much blood from the joints; so it heals therefore either when the wound is more extensive or at the ankle, that it may be cured.
