Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the swellings that are beneath, and the healing through piercing like cutting; and let the fester.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If they cannot get out of it, then put the foot in the water, and let the vein be well-drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	If the veins are not right for the first time, then restart them again a little above, because they are salty; do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and do it similarly with the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle, and its opening is worth the pain in the heel when it's cut.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	If the veins in the ankle are tied so that the patient goes into the bath, and the vein is extracted above the ankle, twist it four times, because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then cut it in all ways you can, and cross-extract it; and use caustic as much as possible, because the veins are very sensitive, and they are greatly distended by hand movements.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find the truth, then a healthy person will have some rain on the foot or back of the leg, and towards the small toe, and ward off the nerves; and make as much care to the wound that you see, and then loosen the ligament, and put cotton on it and tie; now she is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of the sainies of suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or nails, or glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and attracting the wound, or by piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction, which is done by piercing, is in two ways: either it is applied all over the fire, or with fire; and suction that is made by piercing and extracting the wound is done in thirteen places of the body, so that one is on top of the head, and others are around the neck; and two others are on each side of the neck; and there is a ventouse under the chin; and a ventouse between the shoulder blades; and a ventouse above the ribs; and the ventouses in between the two arms; and the ventouses at the knees; and the ventouses on the elbows; and the ventouses on the calves; and suction does not treat of wounds, unless for small veins that are scattered throughout the body, and because of this they do not weaken me, as if I were draining a vein; and it is not suitable to apply it, neither with all fire nor with piercing, in any disease that comes from overstuffing, until every part of the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and myself also when I am in my prime, we command our servants to come and make an opening after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sickness of the mouse is very helpful for the swelling of the head … which comes to the eyes, and it should not be done at all except after the evacuation of all the body; and this opening is in place of the spleen's surgery, and it should not be done by anyone who has cold complexion or stomach issues, because it causes great harm; and therefore they do not recommend using it, nor those who have swelling of the head with cold-related illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blind, and therefore they should put the opening a little lower by the doubt of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wound on the neck is in place of the vein of the head and basilica, and for that it is worth the constriction of the wrist, and splitting of the channel of the forearm, and toasting, and repletion; and they must not press too much, because if she holds too tightly, so the obliquity or stomach and or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wound on the neck has two costels as well as pain of the head, eyelids and emigraining, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you instruct the master to press his hand when placing, so he does not hit the artery, and does not come in any further bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wound below the chin is worth a mouth disease, and corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the wounds of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wound of the shoulders is equal to the disease that comes from cold and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wound of the sides is equal in value as three large veins of the arm, because it causes blood loss from these big veins; instruct the lord to not cut too deeply into the flesh, for the thin skin is bare of fat, and knows beneath muscles and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is equal in value to the emoroids of the fundament, and to other diseases below, it is necessary that the wound be large and filled with pus, for it must be properly treated; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds on the legs heal completely, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are equal to old pains from the rain, and from the belly, and from the bladder, and cause the flowers; and are like two spleens, and two knees, wherever they go, they weaken the body after a long time, and bring on pallor in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Instruct the patient to put on the ventouse first empty, then suctioning at the same time, and place it hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease doing so until you see the blood flowing red and swollen, and applying the redness to the wound; then fasten, and remove the ventouses, and be careful in the arrangement of the bodies, because there are those who have such a strong fever, and cold pores: it is necessary to prick once only, and it is fitting to make large wounds, and shallow ones as well; and suction lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the one without is large, then it is fitting to prick twice: once first to subside the great swelling of the big wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the one without is very thick, it is fitting to prick a third time; and when our wills are satisfied with picking at the small wound little by little, then we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	Instruct the patient to let the blood flow freely, so often renew it; and if it is thick, then prick firmly at the root, and complete as much as possible without perceiving the pains suddenly, and cover with oil from apertif dissolutive: if this is the case, use oil of violet, or oil of almonds sweet, or oil from sesame seeds; and if this is in yever, use oil of cresson, or lemon, or camomile, or similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the flow is large and cold, take oil of amber, or balsamite, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If those whose wounds have large pores, do not apply oil to them, but wash with water from rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, then they rise from that place, or from the water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large discharges rise from old wine, or water of juniper, or annetroot decoction, or camomile, and similar things; and they do not wish to be treated with a ventouse before the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and they do not sleep afterwards, and must wait until they must be ventosed, when it is ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware that he who recovers is choleric, and his stomach is too hot and inflamed; so let him take cold things, such as pears, grapes, endives, lettuce at a gentle pace, and similar things; and eat small pieces, and broth of veal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil,
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles qui sont mises sur le foie, et sur la mouse, et podagre, et sur le ventre et la boude et les rains et l'hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie de ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que pour attirer sang de meme a meme, si com nous mettons sur les mamelles quand le nez saine; pour oster la viscousite qui est au meme, si com nous metons ventouses sur le ventre et sur la boude pour allumer le meme; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l'opilation, ou desaerter la piere de son lieu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sur le foie et sur la mouse quant il i a ventosite retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides pour sucier tant soleillement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensemble feu, et aucunes fois plaines d'aigue tede, si com en maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c'on emplisse la ventouse d'aigue chaude sole, ou d'aigue ou il ait cueit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum given to the fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there should be two fingers of length and half a palm in width from top to bottom, with one finger at the middle, like piercing an arrow, so that it does not wound the patient when putting on the limb; and have in the middle a transverse rod of iron or wood, for holding a cloth wrapped around, and they should be big and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and thinner ones are used for thin people and thicker ones for fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you must put this vacuum on the limb: take a cloth of wax or linen and put it in the middle of the vacuum through the rod that is in the middle of the vacuum, so that the air be at the bottom of the vacuum and does not burn the patient; then put it on the limb, and place your two fingers as we have said, so that when you take it, if there is vapor, it goes away, and remove the vacuum; and take the linen as before, and repeat it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of a coughing patient suffering from pleurisy, has no pain or fever, and does not have vomiting or diarrhea, and is brought to bed only when they are in pain, and placed on the limb alone, and it is this form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	No ulcers are brought to treatment only in limbs or where one cannot put a catheter for the weight, such as lips and gums, and similar ones; and when their noses are cut off, such as two or three, and other similar ones; and the quality of using them is that whenever you find ulcers they are in clean, clear water without pain, take them; and place one in sweet water, so long as they become familiar with it, and have nothing in the belly; and then be dressed from vein and catheter, then rub the limb until it's red, and put on ulcers; and when they are full, and come out, if that can be done to them, then put one back, because this is very good after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	Se ceu non, si leve le leu d'aisil, and then of water, very well, and then the expectation; and if his limbs are too healthy after the wound, cover him with a damp cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on, until he is cleansed; and if they swell, put vitriol crushed or vinegar, and similar things, until they are cleansed; or you put on the limb one-fourth of peeling feathers, and let them be there until they dry out, now he will be cleansed; and if you have more need, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices do not take, then rub the limb with fresh salt, or you prick it with an arrow until the poultice comes out, and then put it on; and as soon as they feel the wound, they dry out; and when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle some powder of alum and millet flour, or ashes, so that they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This book of fractures begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The art of medicine requires many of these operations, for restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the knife surgery is unknown to these books, and no one has read or studied them; and because of this, the science has been lost in our land, for I have not found a good doctor anywhere; and I know nothing except by studying the ancient books, where I have dealt with the knowledge, and through experience, and by my daily routine; and I have described here what is contained, condensed at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sum of our words and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and remain silent on the matter, so that those who have experienced it learn and acquire this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting occurs on anyone, it is necessary to hasten to heal the patient from one part and the other, so as not to cause any further harm if they are weak in body, or sick, or elderly; or if their blood vessels are too tense, or too cold; and avoid eating hot food, such as cool meat, and do not consume any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with too much rich food that fills the veins with blood, until you have some doubt of a severe infection, or of the spreading of matter to the member; if you revive the patients on the first morning after using them.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is fitting that one nourishes the patient with foods that cause great swelling, such as wheat cooked in broth, and fat, and liver, and eggs, and pottage of vegetables, and porridge, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	But when there is swelling because of nourishment, the fracture appears more soon after.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old people and those who are decrepit cannot be well mended or soldered according to their nature because of dryness of limbs, nor can those that are too soft, like bones of small children; but there is no cure. Instead, fix a large splint on the broken bone until it heals and joins with the limb together, as much as possible, and do not leave it without doing its work, and for this reason, they must nourish themselves with great meats, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are different in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fractures of the head are different from those of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that happen from being twisted, and others from cutting, just as the thickness of a hair to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and another where the bone has only a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own tool and instrument for restoration, according to what is remembered in its proper place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone can be detected by how the joint is twisted, and opened well by force, and feels like pressure on the finger; but when there is no twist or turn at all, and the patient does not feel great pain, unless there is a point of fracture; but they can still have twists, splits, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting to move your hand at all, but apply medicines that come after this, and then restrain it now with subtlety.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that if there is a fracture in the arm and two of the joints are separated, it must now be put in straight equal parts, so that it can heal with ease; and if it becomes inflamed, let it remain still for one day until it becomes calm again; then place it evenly on your own muscles so that you can feel it lightly and firmly, and know that restoring the joints is more easy than restoring those where there are pieces; then restrain it, as it seems fitting afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and two parts are pulled out, whether it is a large piece or a small one on your hand, or two cords, or one cord and on your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are missing, you must gradually make up for them with the muscles where you can, and take care that through your work it does not cause the patient additional injury or pain; and add well both joints of the bone in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient feels well in his hand if it seems that he is not well: if he straightens it up and does not strain himself too much, and does not press so as those do who make him come by their own operation with a hot and painful contraction to the member, just as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a point, if you chaste well the patient so that he does not move, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and be sure that the limb is settled so tightly that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	But when he feels no pain, it is not at a point, and one must put him in such disposition that he feels no pain; and be sure to set the limb correctly so that tortuousness does not come upon him when restored, and as for the qualities of the broken member, they are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The body part that is broken is of different smallness, size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	There are small members, such as arms and thighs: the smaller ones, so that they can be wrapped in soft and thin cloths; and the larger ones, like legs: they should be wrapped with a wide and hard bandage, because large bands encircle the entire large member, and press it evenly on all parts, without leaving any gap; then tie soft ropes around it three times or four according to the limb, and tighten it with one hand around the whole bandage, then go up to the top of the break and tighten it less, until the break moves a little bit away from its place; and gradually loosen the bandage piece by piece, so that you take hold of a large part of his healthy tissue, then put another bandage, and turn back above the broken limb; then return to the lower part of the break, and tighten it moderately, not too hard or too soft, as we have said in the previous article; then put cloths between the bands, so that they are all equal, then tie everything with a strong thread from above, and then put your stitches well made, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it has an abscess or an abscess, put up a soothing poultice, and if it thwarts the swelling, and lets it be for some days; then strain the sinews, and sew them with a moody thread of one inch width, or of a beam from which planks are made, or palm trees cut into strips, according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread which one puts on the break is a little larger and wider than the others; and so long as it suits the limb of small or great size; then tighten up the sinews just as you did at the first suture, and tie over them with a strong thread, just as in the first suture above the fracture; the tighter they are, the looser; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and of fine linen cloth; for if the thread is too thick, as I have wanted to make work on foolish folk who make their sutures with cord threads of fine linen twisted, and this is a great error, because the suture cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and does not suit at all that there should be less than two fingers' breadth between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sick with wounds on the arrows after the extraction in their healthy ones, then put soft cloths of linen or wool around them, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the treatment in this way.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to strain the joints of all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not necessary to put joints on them immediately, but rather after 3 or 7 days, or more according to the swelling and inflammation; and here is the manner of the ancient emplasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsion: take flour that is stored next to the mill wall, mix it with a lot of eggs, and make this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, because it is the common manner of the emplaster restoring fractures in various ways, and even for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other way of applying plaster to restore breaks and dislocations and twists: take arrowroot, lard, vinegar, asefetide, gum arabic, mugat, 10; mirre and aloes, 5; alechil VIIII; and make powder, and mix with honey from ufe; if the complexion of the bone is hot, use this plaster because it has good composition, and restore broken bones quickly, and save more men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of applying plaster that saves twisting: take mugat and viscarmale, 10; mirre and aloes, 7; acacia 6; bolic armenic 10, grind well, and confit with water or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat joints and bones is to tie them together and set the bone, and ease the pain that follows, and use the bone to sew up the break: take a new linen cloth, and apply it in oil, and cook in it, and put on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore the limb, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly aligning the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat the bone that restores it: take dried leaves of fig and terrestrial mulberry, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat the plaster for restoring bone break and for draining the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of silymarin, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, from each one a part; and grind, and mix with wine, and heat the limbs, and mix with moist water of coriander or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of applying plaster is stronger than the first, when an abscess comes to heal on the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of silymarin, and seeds of flax, balaustine, meletite, and sanssouci, and flowers of violets and camomile from each one a part; and grind, and mix with warm water or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras writes in his book that one should not put on a broken limb with plaster made of beeswax and oil, and only this, and he says it must be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to be a good idea to put the broken limb above, in order to restore, things that are dry and warm, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat the wound is to use wool and cheese of old men's intestines, or goose quills, and gum arabic, equal in size, break them up, make an ointment, and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then wait a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that his bone is out of place; if not, do it again by the hand, and if pain comes to the joint, or prurience, in repose, swelling, so haste and apply, and remove the ointment now; take a light cloth, and a sponge wet with sea water, and plunge into water, and lift up the limb, until the itching stops, and the pain is appeased; then let it rest for an hour, and put on a clean linen, moistened in water or oil rose, and tied around a nut, so that you are sure of the abscess being hot; and lay to rest the inflammation of the limb, and may the pain be removed, then resume the subtle jointing, and a little ointment, and do not strain it too much as before; and subtlety until it is sound.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that there is an abscess on the foot and redness and pain and swelling are present, I have already set the bone in all cases, and you must need to apply and bind, if it recovers, as you did first when it was even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member anything of what we have said, if you do not loosen it after three days or four or five, and never after twenty days, as one sees, until the break heals and the joint approaches the bone, then tighten more than before, and fill with fat meat, as I said before; and if you see the limb drying up more than necessary is, know that there will come no help, arise then from hot water and tea, every time when you loosen it, and this for so much as to cut off the swelling of the member, and make haste quickly what those foolish doctors do, who leave the member in pain: that is bad, and if it is an overwork, I see nothing but loosening and putting it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	From different kinds of breakings.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breaks and various shapes, and the causes are determined; for there are breaks that are made by striking with a sword, and the joints are cracked through the entire bone just under it, so as to make a crack or a splinter; and because of this, they are called "haichure" this kind of break.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts through the bone in a direction to pierce upwards, and is called this kind of break "absolute"; and there are two kinds of wounds resulting from these breaks, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a piercing, or a splitting, or a crack in the joint of a bone, or a breaking on the bone of a shoulder, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a persistent break which is near the tendon that is under the bone, or above the bone, and is this wound large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered with the bone in a way as subtle as our hair, and there is a small fracture, and because of this it is called a "capillary" break; and if the wound was made by striking a stone, or falling, or by some similar thing, and the piece of the bone gets lodged inside, and the tendons are stuck together like they do when they heat up the cauldrons on top of them.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, like children's heads; and happenings of all these types of breaks are caused by small pieces being dislocated as if they were stones.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures through the pulling away on them, and the questioning has been done, and by the corruption that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known by this that when the bone is discovered, and you rub above it, if the fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take care for any bad accidents that may occur to the patient, and if you see no such bad accident, as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, swelling, and purple spots, and other similar appearances in more severe dispositions, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a most unlikely accident, and you expect good health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when you meet someone who is ill for the first time, and it's in winter, so you should take out the bone on the 14th day after the full moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, so hurry to take out the bone on the 7th day, otherwise the cloth underneath the bone will become corrupted, and accidents similar to those we have mentioned will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just next to the cloth covering the brain, so that you should cut the fractured part thus: and hold the patient's head tightly, and uncover the bone in all directions that you can, and in such a way as to make the wound as smooth as possible, and if blood comes upon uncovering the bone or abscess, then help it with what is needed, and so you should fill the place of the bone with moist cloths soaked in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess subsides, and be sure of not having any blood; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two methods:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he drinks another dose more than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you should have various numbers of cuttings, some are three and others are large, and they are all pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly so as not to hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is convenient that you pierce into the center, otherwise, so that you administer cuttings with caution, do not puncture more than enough that they penetrate beyond the bone to the skin of the test; and on top of the point there should be a margin or a circle, lest the point go over the bone; and it is convenient to have more, so that each comes out in its own place at the edge of the bone, thus having tarers for all tests; and this is the form of the III kinds of tareres:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the bone that it breaks are that you put there later on the bone, and turn to your two hands until you know when the bone is pierced; then place the later one another part after a little bit of time, and do all around like this, then strike the incisors the space of the bone between the pertu, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take out the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools that you have such as tongs, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the scalp.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, if it covers that which is left behind on the bone at all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more subtle and darker than the other incisors; and if there is nothing of the small bones or scales, take them lightly with one of the tools; then cure the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another manner of work is thus: as the Gauls say, which is more true; and it is strongly said, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone, where or at the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you place below the head of this incision lens-shaped, because it is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is weak in two sides, so that the cutting is to the bone; then with a small hammer above, so that you lightly copy the bone all around, and you be well guarded of the fabric below; if it is rough against the bone, you lightly remove the bone, for one removes the bone without much pain, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone of the break has not been pierced through to the cloth, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, so it fits back into that roughness, and removes the scales at the razor-sharp instrument that you must have in various quantities, for each one as convenient, according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have many rough razors and then finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is good.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other types of capillary cuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary to apply caution according to its direction; and this is something that no one else knows who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the syphilitic is uncovered, so it's necessary to apply cloth according to its quantity; and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in II or III, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, that you don't press the syphilitic, but rather apply pressure from above another tie, and not strangle it unless when the wound is healed alone; and leave it for one day or two, until the abscesses are calmed down, then loosen it, and administer medicines such as rose roots, flour of mulberries, and powdered incense, and similar things; and make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer more medicine after mastication; and be careful that the wound is completely cleaned, lest you leave any ointment or reassemble bowels, for when bowels assemble under the cloth of the brain, they corrode and bring great evil to the patient; because when something mordant is put on the syphilitic, it festers from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Wear a bandage then, for if no accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful until there is doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackness does not come back except for the medicine we have placed on it, which has virtue, then it is fitting that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in vinegar I wrap, and put it on him; then apply the treatment of cures as he needs, until he is cured.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two joints are broken at once, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and that bone below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists violently, and then becomes injured.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two joints is broken, it is fitting that you put your small dog or broken bone into the joint, and put the broken joint inside your dog's index finger, and in a pouch for safety, until the joint returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the body and cannot come back to its place, so that you put equal weight on the head of a stick one piece thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do it again and hasten to restore it the first day if you can; but if not, after the seventh or tenth part, when the apses are closed, then be wrapped around the head of the upper body with linen strips, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or wrap the other bandage around it if the break is there; and let the strips be thick enough to fill up the holes in the upper body.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that we must moisten the bandages in butter and apply each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is likely that they are moist in the mixture of wool and water, and powder of millstone; then let them hang, until the bones have hardened, and the cartilage has become tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes put on wool or netting in its place, and if it has a warm covering on top, and holds the wound closed, and blows the patient through it; then make the knife cut that you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to a head while you are working on it, put a coating of vinegar or wet cotton in oil, or in half a pint of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come to a head, put on plaster according to need, made of sown flour and powder of incense, mixed with wool; then place light tiles upon it, and do not tie the wound; and if the breakage is small, and it breaks into small pieces, then extract the necessary instruments for that, and sew the laceration, and treatment of such painful wounds, and stitching, if plaster and bandages are suitable for that; and if there is no wound inside the abscess, then treat with poultices, and put on cans filled with salt, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the surgery of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is cut under, and there is no wound to be found, and only a simple fracture without bone splintering inside, if one notices it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, that you push your two fingers into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then push your two fingers with your right hand, and push the fracture gently inside, and apply pressure to the other hand without one.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is twisted to the second tooth, it is necessary that you manage an extension of two parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth happens, or a fracture, then wrap up with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put the broken mandible on a cloth, and place over a double fold; and put over one a fine stake well made, or a piece of leather even long and wide according to the mandible, and bind it above the teeth that you can, and command the patient to rest, and serve light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then put him in a new bed, and place on it powder from the mill with abundance of water or seme's flour, after what you have extracted the cerote; and put on the plaster linen light, and if the plaster dries, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave him as long as he is cured; many are cured in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes on a limb, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if it has a break and a wound together, repair the broken piece of bone that is extracted; with such subtlety of extraction suitable for these.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it as necessary.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have extracted all these pieces and it does not stay in place, close the wound, if it is wide; and apply suitable dressings to it, in order to heal, as long as it becomes sound.
de la forcele	of the fistula
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fistula often breaks in front of the shoulder, and the break occurs in three manners: either it is broken and separated into two, with fragments, and this is the lightest to repair; or there are breaks with wounds.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Instruct the surgeon to have two assistants, so that one holds the assistant who feels the breaking force, and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then place the break at your two fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to extend further, place over the patient's shoulder a round spear of linen or cloth, so that it is large according to your necessity; stretch and lift the swelling, and strain the spear with your hand, so that you put in equal the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot touch the chief of the swelling outside for fear that it is come to a head, so be it if the patient lies on his hateful side, and place over the shoulder a pillow mean, and have the assistants pour the shoulder downwards, until the bones of the swelling are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the break to your feet, and if you find debris there, it is fitting that you cut into it; and take out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join itself for any sort of swelling, hit one of the incisions that you have made; but make sure to apply force with this instrument, in order to protect the sinew.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not made of bone, and is as large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; having two handles, just as you see them, and one being long and the other short, so that it corresponds to the roughness of the wound you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of cutting into an abscess, cut the wound, and if the roughness is small, or you doubt the size of the abscess, then apply the wound with drapes and tentes, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If the abscess comes out, then apply a poultice made of oil rose, ash, and vinegar on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is to put on the bone the plaster made of flour from the mill and ashes of wood, and light weights upon it, and if necessary, place a spear below it; then take a large bandage one palm wide, and apply double layers of poultice, and plaster; then take a slender stake three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the edge of the bandage is hanging; put the stake above the break, and turn the bandage over onto the shoulder, and below the shoulder, to relieve pain; and repeatedly apply this to both sides until you see the limb hold the break perfectly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move under the broken bone, so be careful each day, and when the limbs are straight, then release the binding; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the shoulder, to lift the plaster above, thus alleviating the swelling by the stretching of the shoulder, or by tying his arm to the neck, and not untying if any bad accident comes, for twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see that it needs to be reapplied, and bind and release it in such a way, until he is restored; and she is restored after twenty-eight days, and less often than at some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of a shoulder fracture.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the break of the shoulder, if it is broken or wrenched, let him not move until he is warmed up by his touch; then repair according to the shape of the break, and remake according to his natural form in all ways that you can; then put on the limb powder made from flour with a lot of water, and light poultices, and place upon it double bandages; then place above an iron bar large but subtle, a little wider than the shoulder, and so take out the bar so that no hair of the poultice sticks to it, if you do so carefully; and then tie him tightly with a big bandage so that the bar does not move from its place, and look at the bond every day; and whenever he swears, tie him again, and put equal the bar when it is out of its place, and give relief to the patient on his side; and the shoulder will be healed in XX days or XXV, And when these numbers are completed, take him off, and let yourself be sure, for it is not the bone that goes back to being light.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points downward from the joint, let them do so, and then above, and make the bone, and do what we have said in breaking down an abscess on the cheek.
de la brisure dou pis	of a broken foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The flesh is rarely broken in the middle, but it happens often outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downward and causes the patient great pain, and lack of appetite, and thirst, and sometimes vomiting blood, and opening the veins on the fractured bone, and the smell is very bad.
