Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and you place a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the two ribs with your hands, and gently put equal pressure in all directions until the bone takes its proper shape; then put in plaster strips and stoves above the subtle piece of salt, or another lighter substance, and wrap it up in one fold, and tie it to the fractured bone so that it does not move; and turn the knot around to the back, and tighten immediately, and reward each hour with a bandage, and if it loosens, re-tighten; and if he wants to be released, because of corrosion or prurite that comes to him, or pain or abscess, you hasten, and release him, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come from cures in such ways; then reattach the plaster, and tighten until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	They know that the breaking of ribs comes only from their big bones behind the back, and in the chest above, and they bend because they are brittle; and it hurts very much to the examination as the reason.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you set the break equal when it is suitable.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a poultice, and bind with a stick, if you have need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the ribs break inward, he feels great pain, and puncture, like pleurisy, because the bone presses against the membrane; and he is filled with pangs, and thirst, and vomits, and suffers great planty of blood, and it's a sign of sickness, and the old men have put much effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if to those who say it is suitable to administer foods that cause swelling in the belly, to put an end to the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this if blood does not come from the incision.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes out, then let it be so.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one should put poultices on the limb to suck out blood, because it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that this will attract the superfluous blood to the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the limb with a linen cloth moistened in hot oil, and put towels between the ribs to keep the joint even, then either apply a treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu'il ne puet soffrir par l'os qui point la toile,
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to bind with moist cloth in oil rose (oil and resin), and put it on low; and cure while the patient has that which needs an abscess, and let him sleep above his chest or where he must, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no fracture of the bones of the neck, and it does not happen when he falls; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens and you know whether he will be healed or not, if you see his hands soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	He who has suffered from more such displacements, and if he is quiet and feels well when one tightens him and holds him back, knows that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will recover, if they are put into a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens at the back of the spine, and you know whether he will recover or not, take care if the feet are softened, and if the accidents are in his hands, and on the back he should jump up with great force and excretion against his will; and when one has put him back onto his stomach, he should jump up again with great force.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is put back onto his stomach and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that he will die: if one does not labor in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the thing is even lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you will reward it if there is an abscess hot, if you put oil of rose or oil from milk of sheep on the spine, until it be appeased; then put on one of the plasters comforting and drying, and bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is fractured, it is fitting to cover the wound; and take out the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are great, with a suture, then apply bandages made from linen cloth, stained with wine, until he is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which are called "heads of the knee", put your left-hand pouch to it, and place it against your right hand, then put on the plaster and the splint, if you have one; then bind it, and if there is a fractured bone, repair it, take out the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the femur
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the femur bone is fractured, and if so, then if it has been for just a little bit of swelling at the head; and let it be long, and incline to the bend, and comes to the patient pain at the joint, and stiffness, and swells as it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are above the fracture; and observe how it is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only in the head alone, then set equal this fracture, so far as it has the natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on his belly, so that the restoration of this fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have made it even, put the plaster on, then put a stake of wood or horn upon it, and bind the fracture, so that it does not move; and apply the plaster beneath the ribs, until they are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his sound side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes up on the foot, do not touch it, until the abscess is calmed down, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and bind as needed, without any additional accidents, this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one between the arm and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of the two methods: for one method is that you take a stick made of wood or horn, in the shape of this figure:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Instruct the patient to tie both shoulders and tighten them up high, and make the patient lie on two sieges; then let the gout burst on the arm broken at the shoulder, until it comes to a swell, and take him an arrow of wood, then push upon any heavy thing or the ministers stretch it out to the end; then put the mire into the swelling equal to his hands together, until the swelling returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that you should put the patient on his back, and tie his hand to his neck, then command both ministers to have each one pull in this way: one pulls up above the wound with his hands, and the other pulls down below all the ligaments, and stretch out each one to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then tie down all the ligaments below the wound and above the wound, and stretch out each one of the ministers to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	In case of a fracture close to the shoulder joint, it is necessary that you put in place the middle ligament under the bone, and the other one towards the cut; and similarly, if the fracture is near the cost, so that you put in place the lighter ligament without labor, until the fracture is even on its own position and on its side; then set straight the fracture as it seems proper, and tie it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If the abscesses come, do not tie it immediately after seven days; instead, put a linen cloth in it and oil rose, until the abscesses are calmed down; then tie it, and the manner of tying is that you place plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or its side; put a bandage on, and tie above the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm stays in its place, unless any thing prevents it, or if the bones are not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone moves, then use needles, and place a larger and stronger needle on the break than the others, and have two spaces between each needle, and so one space should be three times as large as each other; then strain over the needles, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the needles and straining, as we have said, in the wound where you restore the broken member, and you doubt whether the abscess is infected, and if you leave it for seven days, just as we have said; then observe each of three days the tie that forms, when it prurites or swells there will not be life in the flesh, or there will come swelling to the limb because it is too strained.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If he will, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents happen, and he does not loosen his bandage after three days or more, and rests on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and puts the cloth under the shoulder with one big piece of linen evenly, and looks at each hour of the day, whether the broken figure of the member moves or softens the ligaments; and he follows the advice by the virtue of medicine, and gives him the meat which we have put before him in such a way that the meat is softened; and when it begins to take nourishment, if it is still difficult.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary to return the cloth and the leg after forty days of all treatment, then he must be loosened and given bath and medicines for the joint to be made healthy.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is crooked and swollen, it will stay for three or four days.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "fossicles", one small and that one which nourishes the pouch (the fat pad); and the other large one, which is below the smaller one; sometimes it is only the larger bone that breaks alone, or sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the smaller bones are broken, healing is lighter and faster; but when the larger ones break, it's a poorer healing and more grievous than if both were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the smaller bone is broken, it's better to extend it lightly and put it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If it's the great frost, then they must strain it more strongly; and stretch out to the cleft, and tighten the pouch of the hand higher than others, and pull the fingers lower than others, and so that the patient crosses his own leg, and stretch towards himself, and cry before him higher, that the patient may not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's one arm to the part below to his hand, or at the joint, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put him in the mirror, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is in pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is no need to pull or bind it tight, since you cannot restore it to its proper place, then take out the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break he has an injury, I have spoken to the singular chaper about it; so take the care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, if pus appears at the wound, then apply a dressing made from rose oil and white beeswax, not too hard nor too soft; and tie up the dressing gently, until the pus is appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the rose oil, and mix the plaster from powdered flour with a lot of water; put the splints, and make the splint over the break stronger, and slightly larger than the others; and notice that it must have six splints or more, depending on the situation: whether the break is in one bone or two; and tie it tighter above the break than elsewhere, and always less when removing, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the dressings be soft and moist over the break, not too hard nor harsh; and make the threads, from which it is strained, of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accidents occur to the limb, just as it pricks at the limb, so that they be appeased; and let the limb not be too tightly restrained from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the straitening, and when the ligaments are loosened and the bones set in place, and it seems so, then direct.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it is found that the swellings cannot come to the limb because it is too tightly straitened, so that it be loosened a little, and let it rest for some days, until the swelling subsides, then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If no such thing happens as we have said to the patient, nor if he is freed from his troubles within twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And when he is questioned further, then let him put his hands on his neck, and if their necks are even, and he guards against movement and digging, and sleeps on his back; and you know that this breakage will be restored in thirty days or forty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the properties and the nature of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of a hand break.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand there is often little breakage, and only pain occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the finger of the hand is broken or sprained, if it is fitting that the patient tie crosses, and sit straight in front of him always; then put his hand on an extended stool, and stretch out the broken limbs, and set the joints equal to the fingers, until they are well joined; and apply plaster and bandages, unless there comes any abscesses, and then tie an arrow according to the quantity of blood that flows; and wrap it up in 1 yard of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	In the event of a fracture in the tendons near the inside of the foot, do thus: make an arrow of cloth and command the patient to bind it to his broken tendon; and then tie it with a rope for a long time so that the wound is as large as the injured finger, and let it be tied thus as seems proper.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the space, it is fitting that you place a splint above and another below the foot, so that the fingers are straightened and made right, then bind all around the hand, and secure the tie between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of us of the two fingers, and it is swollen, then let it be flattened, as seems proper; bind with the hand, and if you see that putting a small straight splint to lift the fracture will not move, and if the fracture is in the other finger, place it on the index or one of the others, so that it flattens, and secure it with the healthy finger next to it; or tie them all together, as long as possible, either by putting a splint above, or as you wish; take care in restoring and arranging the abscess, and heal those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the cube is broken
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the cube is often broken, and it can be seen when they turn in front and behind; and the restoration is that one ties up above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lie on their face, then each minister extends his ties equally to both sides; and this is when the break is inside the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the cube, then one ties to the arm and the other ties below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the joint, and then so either one ties to the joint or one extends below; then put the splint on the bone equally with its two hands, until it corresponds to its natural figure, and then apply plaster, and bandage, since abscesses never come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has an abscess, so let it be appeased first, and then return to its work and treatment; the release is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap a bandage around the wound with two or three bands doubled in II or III, and leave the swelling; then turn the leg so that the toes reach to the root of the nail, and pour I long thread between the thigh and the leg, under the knee, and put the head of the thread above; then turn up the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then apply stitches to the wound, and place a stitch on the bone of the leg; then wrap soft cloth around between the leg and thigh for equal tension, and begin to tie form III twists or IV on the wound; and as you go higher up on the wound, and less it binds; then put as II threads of the thread that you have poured between the leg and thigh, and apply III stitches that are above, then return under the head of the thread, until you see from below at the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then let it be so, and if it comes to no more swelling, no inflammation, or any similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if it has happened, so that the dislocation occurs and address it as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone caught in it, then they should be pulled out; and if you cannot, then it is necessary to split the limb and cut open; and the treatment will be like what we have said, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in that manner as we put in nails, so as in the shoulder and on the arm; all are well, in the restoration done thus there is no lock of the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And after three days or slightly less or more, according to the diversity of the complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the vein in the groin.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The joint of the elbow is prone to breakage, but it bends multiple times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, but only forms a crack or separation, and is prone to all wounds, pain, and causes great suffering.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is as follows: if you put equal pressure on what has been broken at its two ends, until it is assembled again, when can be done; then apply plaster, and put an rounded splint, if necessary, and bind as it needs to be bound; afterwards restore all the dispositions that we have said on other breaks, such as abscesses or similar things; for each accident that he needs, until he is cured.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	If there are two bones in the leg, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other is called "foscile", then all breakages occur like it does when it comes to the arm; and because of this, the restoration is done equally, and the wounds are entirely healed. And if the two bones are broken together, so turn the leg from every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bones are broken, then turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then feel great pain and see it well; and turn downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then apply extension, and set it equal, and tie the strings equally; but whenever there are broken bones, it is necessary to adjust them according to their value; and make the deformed one lighter.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when you have completed your work, so take two faxes of wood that pain the leg from one side and the other, and are long as the length of the leg from knee to ankle; then wrap it around both legs and tie it at the middle, and at this binding the leg cannot turn either to the right or to the left, and thus is good; and none should administer bandages of that length to the leg, nor use wax, and put on the leg to ward off movement, and properly done in the break where it has been injured; and move each one every day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; so do this until the cure is sane.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone break at the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but sometimes at the two-foot joint a fracture occurs and it is painful, and in some cases there is fear of further breakage.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If he has a fracture of the two-foot bone and you see these bones overlapping one another, place this patient on the ground, just as if he were running, and then place your foot upon his own, so that when the bones are raised, press them thus until they align in their place; then apply plaster and strips to it, and place a small wooden splint with two pegs under his foot; then bind him firmly with cloth, and other things of which you may need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if the bandage is released, because you will find that the bones are in place, whether they are fractured, dislocated, or swollen.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If he has any broken bones, then remove them, and set them, as we have said about the broken bones of the hand; then put a splint on the broken bone according to its length, and make it slightly larger, then place over the foot that is painful, as I have said; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then put a splint on each one according to its quantity, wrapped in a bandage of linen, and bind the foot under the leg; and while standing above the head of the table, so that the belly is over the foot, he will be well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is fitting that you do not forget the other things I have said about other broken bones, since we have spoken of them; and cure each injury as becomes.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's body breaks, if she sits on it and enlarges, then incline her to that part at the back, and keep it behind; then fill the wound with cotton as I have said, and put there also a larger quantity like this one; then bind her, lift her back piece by piece, and then squeeze the cotton, until it comes to the opening of her body, and the bone returns with the stuffing; and when she urinates, if there is still some cotton, and when she has finished urinating, take it out, and so do this for seven days or more: if she will be restored, then take a vessel of wool, tie to the broken one a rope, and pour all the vessel into her body; then blow through the rope until the vessel is filled inside: thus the bone will return. Then fill with cotton again and let it be as I have said for some days, until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the finger is broken in the man or woman, restore it as we have said with the bone of the heel; and do not conceal these nearby breaks near the one who puts his study and use on them, and attend to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks mean more frequent deaths on the right path of restoration; then attend.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the phallus when it is broken, take an owl's gizzard and inject the phallus into it; then wrap the cloths around, and let it rest for three days or more, and it will be healed soon.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has breaks with wounds, especially if it is great, just as if the bone of the scapula or shoulder joint or similar were broken, that he be made whole now, provided that the remedies we have stated testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is healing well, then apply vitriol again if you have nothing else, and then recommence to restore the break in that same hour, or on the next day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes, then leave the restoration until next day, as long as it is allayed, and do not touch it or on the third day or the fourth, because you will cause bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone break is appearing near the joint of the elbow, it is advisable to let you put it at an easy point with a slight touch in your hands.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension does not fit to be placed at an equal point with your hands, using that instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight inches long, and the size is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary to the surgeon to press three or four times, according as he has need in each cure of fracture; and it should be round and one small, so it does not bend under compression on the member at your work, and it should be big in front, and one inch from the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the bowed shoulder must be placed on top of the visible bone; and let the water boil once, until it returns, and so that they are even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the splints cannot well grasp the bone, so that it may have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then let it be done by one of the instruments that are suitable for this, such as a knife or saw, to your power; and then take out what remains in the bone with roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain after, recognize that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you let it be in its place, then cut out the diseased part in wine-stained vinegar, and properly clean it up; and do not put any ointment on the wound or anything else there, unless it brings pus and corruption; then administer salves when you have restored the bone, and expose the wound, and cover everything with a covering according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound does not become strained with the break; and many fools have done this, and have brought on the patient death or corrosion sometimes; and so are the straining actions more mild and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that anything worse will come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so that it cannot be put on any salves; but instead wrap it around, with bandages, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two the swelling of the bone above the wound, then see that which you have put there to all wine, and apply salve to heal wounds, just as salve tetra-foam and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb two times a day, morning and evening, until it is cooled and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be prepared in such a way that the swelling goes down freely.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it happens every day and the swelling does not come down but instead comes again with swollen bone, see that there are small pieces of bone, because this is why you must cover the wound with a splint, and remove all these little pieces of bone which cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the joint, or another kind of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he said in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens up in the limb, like the bone of the chest or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large members, do not treat it immediately, because many die from it, but let it happen until it heals; perhaps it will die after 20 days or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can; if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come on account of soddeness.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	These often come after the health of the fracture, most especially when it is near the joint, and it's a terrible thing to see the figure of the limb; and sometimes it cannot be done that the limbs are set right naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient then so that if he is fresh: if the minister gives him medicinal medicines such as aloes, incense, and mirror, and saffron, aconitum, and similar other things, and you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with vinegar medicinal or with many wine or with oil; and put on the nut in poultices, and tie it well, and do not untie it in hands daily; and then loosen it, and repeat another one until the knots are drawn out; or you strain on a piece of plonc well made; for the property of the plonc is that it removes all the swellings above the members; and if the knot is converted into hardness like stone, and it is needed to draw it out, so take away the one from above, and make the obvious protrusion apparent; or you bring it back to any rasping, until it is drawn out, and the cure until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	One weak member after a guard
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored and stays after the weak members and subtle movements, it happens for many reasons: because one is due to being too tightly tied up, and was not loosely tied as it needed; or because there are too many ties, and cannot come to the member; or because of excessive swelling; or because of great movements, but not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the swelling in him multiplies; and administer a bath, and give joy and ease to the patient; then put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts great swelling, and the swelling often comes from standing in wet places, until the swelling reaches the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One twisted limb after healing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and bones break apart, and the form of the limb is ugly, it is essential to not give up on its natural healing process: do not believe false people who say you should break the limb anew, for many foolish men have done this in our land; and these injuries are condemned, and often lead to great evils, and sometimes death. Whenever nodules and torture are fresh, it is advisable to apply hot water or to cook herbs like valerian, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and to make a plaster that softens like aqua lion well done, and take the muscilloid of valerian, and mix with lard or sesame oil, and make the plaster on; or you take figs greased, and grind them with flour of colon, and similar medicines that ease the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is there an obstruction of the nose because it is constantly rubbed continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let you move each limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if torticollis is old and hardened, like stones, and the need is to apply heat with iron, if you think it's advisable to cover just beneath the bone with a subtle incision lightly; and put on a cushion and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This is the beginning of the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, so they must now set it straight again.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells up and sometimes if it is put back in place by pain; for that reason they should not move it until it has swollen down: many times this has led to phlegm and other pains; however, when it happens, one must set the patient right, then let him go, as long as the swelling is gone; then arise the limb with hot water and oil, then set it back lightly, and cure each member as soon as the treatment comes in its own way.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocation of the head into ten pieces.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jaws are displaced to and fro, and the dislocations of both sides occur in two manners: or they are a little bone loose from its place, and softened a little; or they are completely displaced, and falling towards the chin, and bursting open the salivation of the mouth so it cannot be closed, nor can it close its mouth, and is overcome with speech with the tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns in multiple positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and completed, you must quickly reset them; do not delay. And in such a manner that the doctors apply the head of the patient to the dislocation, and pour into one of his hands a small amount from one of its fingers into the root of the mandible inside the mouth, since the dislocation is two parts; and hold off with the other hand, so as not to spoil, and command the patient to relax his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physicians put equal weights on both sides, until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if they return stiff, especially when it is the two lower mandibles assembled, apply hot water and oil until the returns are light; do not worry about returning them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned equally and the patient's mouth is closed with a soft mold, made of moist cloth in a rosin-oil mixture, then tie it gently to the molten joints; and put the patient on his back, and his knees between two couches, so that he does not move his head or right arm nor left arm, nor tries to straighten himself, but takes light meat until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are healed; then take what he wants lightly, and do not work on opening the mouth to feed and drink, until the mandible is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not converted back to their own shape, then fever and chills occur, and by chance, a solution of the stomach, and by chance, vomiting pure.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it's fatal; and many times die the one who has it within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the elbow
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The elbow cannot be dislocated over the costal area within the joint and in the pit, and is often unsuccessful without fail, and it can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and stretches out his arms; and then presses the joint to the palm of his hand, and it returns; then applies the plaster and the bandage, and binds it; and the wrist which was on the side cannot be dislocated if not so, and if it dislocates at all, he must reset it to its place, as we have said; then applies the plaster and the bandage, and binds it, and commands the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way, bring back the elbow when it is restored to its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways that the shoulder is dislocated: one way it dislocates at the lower end of the bone below; and another at the lower part of the arm bone; and sometimes it dislocates above, which rarely happens; and does not occur behind the shoulder or inside near the joints; but more often dislocates downwards towards the lower end of the bone, especially in people who are weak, because it occurs suddenly; in those with a moderate amount of strength, it occurs at the joint itself, while in those with good strength, it occurs at the ends.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some people that there is a blow or a crushing injury, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with a swollen abscess, and they think it has been dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary therefore that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they fall down to the shoulder joint, and you will find a difference between the diseased and healthy shoulders, and you will discover between them manifest differences; and you will find in the head of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder joint at the top of the shoulder, just as if it were an open wound; and the patient cannot bring their hand to its normal position or move any limb; and so, if they are displaced upwards, they are not concealed, because you can see them clearly in the upper part; and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to set when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	Instruct the patient to let his hands rest above, then put your fingers below the wrist, and raise the joint at force above in the hand; and the minister raises the hand, and extends it above since he puts it below; if it happens soon.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in the hands, after four days, it is advisable for the patient to be bathed in hot water; and let him take a mild and soothing remedy, like a decoction of altes and fenugreek and mellilote in hot water, and let it be given. Then sit the patient on his back, and put a cloth with an equal number of linen threads above the wound, neither too soft nor too hard; then place the fingers of the other minister on the cheek of the patient, so that he does not move; this shoulder will return to its normal position, and if you see it again according to this method: and it is for you to make the patient be present with one man who is larger than the patient; and let him stand up straight towards the cost, and pour some water into the armpit of the patient, and lift the arm above so that the patient hangs in the air; and the other minister treats the hand of the patient upwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is very light, so that with him there is no heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And also to recover it in another way: and is on striking a long iron rod into the earth, where the head of the joint is also repaired like an arrow, but not too big or too small; then put down below the patient, but if he has wrapped himself soft beneath, and his joints are standing firm with this long stick; then extend his hand away from that side, forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not return by all those things which we have said, then do this cure: take a rod of two arms wide and four fists long, which has the head right behind for penetrating into below the bone, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie under the head of the fist so that it does not hit the face, then place it below the flesh of the patient; and stretch out some arms above the fist of the long one, and tie the assistant above the fist, and the arm to the head of the hand; then put the arm on the side of an eschiele with a large size, and let the hands stretched down, and leave the body hanging from another part: the joints are restored now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in that state, however you do it, if it suits to put below the skin an arrow of wool equal, then place the bandage around the eschiele with an emplaustre prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and myrrh of beeswax, on both shoulder and back; then pull apart below the skin immediately, and turn the tie on the bandage, and encircle the hand to its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	Instruct that the treatment is done slowly, until the limb is comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then do again after 5 days or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healing.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen due to moisture that has come upon it, or for another reason, it is proper that you administer cauterization at three punctures, as it is placed in front of or near the cauterization instrument.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do this and the joint does not stay in place after 7 days, and it cannot lift up one arm above, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint was never fixed in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the foot and knees, or behind, is done by force and stretching of hands, and another joint is used to treat it; and care should be taken until he is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes to afflict the limb again and moves slowly, so that the patient uses baths many times until the affliction is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation from the cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Says that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; and when it has been dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and dislocations do not cure because one can see it well and feel it well; and they dislocate according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, if you can see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is fitting that you reset it so that the abscess forms again, because if the abscess had formed at this time, it would have caused greater grief; and by chance, it cannot be reset entirely, especially when it is on the back; therefore, this is worse than other dislocations, causing more pain, and by chance, death comes to it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is done when it can be reset in such a way that you stretch out both of your hands to meet its hands; and his arms are spread out, and the fingers are pulled according to the costure inward and outward, and thrust into the joint at its joints and base, or at the root of its palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation, so that it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the root of the palm which is loosened.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, so that one administers a strong extension; and two men extend the arm, and two men wrap it around the arm, so that it does not move with the extension; then turn the arm of each part, after you have wrapped a double-length and wide cloth around it; and when the joint aligns itself with the jointed limb, apply some oil to soften the joint, then make the joint firm, until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply plaster on top with some oil, and tighten the bandage, and let it stay for a few days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the ligament and let it go; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it go again for a few days, until it is firmly fixed; then loosen.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels great pain after the return of the joint, and it remains still, then bathe and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or put on a fatty mutton plaster over the joint, let it stay for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint temperamentally, then put back the plaster, and then let him enter the bath again; and do this twice or thrice until he is cured; and if you see, put on a wet and hot fennel poultice with butter, and strain over it; and if it returns to its condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
