Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than the others. In all cases, it must be returned to its original place immediately, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the limb becomes swollen or a foul odor develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when returning it is that you put the diseased hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the other hand, and straighten the nails, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and presses down until it returns To all cases, it must be observed whether it is well in its place; then put the patient's back of his hand on a table at extension and at returning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if there is a dislocation of the hand on the back, then instruct the patient to place their shoulder on the table, and look at that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if it comes back now, then it is well; for if the pressure of poultices calms down abscesses and wounds, and he leaves himself so as to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you do not put him back into place after some days, then the joint will remain twisted; and there is no advantage for the patient except that his hands are swollen, and he cannot stretch or strain anything more; and therefore you know that the nerves have been struck, or the arteries; if there is no other solution except to apply cauterization in the case, and by chance it may be better than nothing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are at rest, place the plaster on that which we have said, then strain it and leave for four days, then remove and leave as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well and there is no pain, place the poultice of hot water upon it, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the elbow of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never are the elbows of the hand displaced in one direction only, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; so you must tighten it and push the dislocation into your pouches until it comes out, then support the joint of the elbow, and turn towards the side where it is displaced; and leave for two days, and then put the bandage on that day; do not tie it, as we have said, and release it from day to day, and move it loose, and secure it again, and do this repeatedly until it is tight, and just as we did before, if it has been displaced on the belly of the hand, and do so in the same way until it is healed; and do the same when it is displaced in another direction.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Because of the shoulder is dislocated.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or the neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, if there is no remedy, because death rushes to the sick.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that it cannot be held in place, and often some member becomes soft or the two arms or one arm and sometimes the dislocated shoulder moves into four parts; this which moves to the back is called "gilbositez": the cure knows that if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no remedy or healing altogether.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And this one that comes from a fall or blows or similar things: they used to say old remedies with big words, and had no great gain; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I dis that in the goutiness that comes to the toe before, no gain nor strength is found; and as it also comes straight on to two sides, and cannot be cured with fire unless those who come straight to the back are treated properly, as I say; and because the patient must be stretched out face down to an equal place, and have of a strain below him, so that he does not bleed; then put one stone at his head in the ground firm, and another on the other side of the joints of the malady, and tie one rope behind the knees of the malady, and another around the hams and knees, and also around the feet, and so two ministers will see to the ropes, one at the head and the others at the sides, between the two stones; and they must be well closed, like we have said, and the mires must put her palms on the stone sharp, until it turns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if she does not return by this cure, take an iron bar of three cubits long, and shave the bone under it, and let the patient lie on his side, and strike the head of the bar against the bone, then place the midpoint of the bar on the spine; and put your fingers in your other hand on the other end of the bar, and press well, until he returns to life; and if you see this, do it to the turnip that turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And so you fix two pins in the head of the patient with one arm's length of wood, and between two other pins, and place them over the joints, about an inch above and below, so that each pin has one nail through it, or the turnip is turning, and the nails are firmly set in the ground so they do not move; and between two pins have one pin turning, because the nails of both turns turn, and between two turns have two small nails one inch long to make the turnip turn again; and then tie the ligature which is among the joints to the turnip towards the head, and another ligature towards the feet to the other turnip, and each minister turns his turnip all along the ligature, and the master places the spine level as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Et quant elle est igalz, si met sur emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc,
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the knee
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is understood that the knee and shoulder joints only come to dislocations, not to other kinds of joint problems; and the knee joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and before and behind; and it is more dislocated on one side than the other, and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And one who knows about dislocations inside says that when a sick leg is joined to a healthy one, it will be longer, and the patient's knees will be more open than those of the healthy person, and they cannot double their knee movement by heating; because the ones who are near the swelling from an abscess are hot, for this is why the head of the shoulder comes loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one whose illness comes to pass, is when this injury is contrary to those that occurred before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one whose it happens in front, is that he stands well his leg according to completion; all goes, do not double the knee towards pain, and if he wants to be made to walk, does not come before, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he walks, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one whose it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double, and this leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin has softened, and the joints of the pelvis are loose below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation is that if you repair since the dislocations are ancient and they stay according to their nature, without any cure; and it is not advisable for him to have hope.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In this case that occurs when the dislocation is fresh and it's one of four types of dislocations, so hurry up and turn the joint and push it inside and prevent further injury, in case it reoccurs, there's no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, if you should apply a strong minister to it and fix the leg with two hands, or at one strap so that it's tied above the knee; and another type of minister extends his hand upwards like this, so that he pours blood from under his armpits, then tightens an apron-like ligature on the chest; and others tie the head to the ligature; and they extend all upward and downward once, until the patient is lifted up once, and remains.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common among four types, and if a dislocation has occurred, as we have said, it is very good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If it is not so, then it is advisable to apply treatment to its resemblance When dislocations occur in the joints, it is advisable that you elevate the patient on their cost side, then put a bandage around the joint, and the one below the angle, then tie the bandage up towards the angle, and towards the flesh; then take hold of another servant and enfold the large bandage of the malady's elbow, and stretch it away from the form: if it returns to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in that manner as we have said, then it is advisable to tie the two feet of the malady together with a strong bandage on both heels and knees; so that the ill limb is extended twice as much as the others; then hang it from the head of a post, and above the ground two arms long; then command one minister to enfold the head of the elbow, and let another minister be tied alongside with the malady, who enfold together: for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are at the door, treat the patient as we have said in the one with goutiness, and pull out the ligament above the diseased leg properly, and above the joint too; then put two splints, one on the head and one on the knee, then stick a splint between the bones of the patient who has this form; and apply moist cloths around it so that the patient does not bleed, then stretch out each of these servants to him, and tie the ligament evenly with his hand to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, put on the splints, and place the patient on a surface, and press in such a way as we have said in the case of goutiness, and treat the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocation occurs before it, you should extend the ill leg as quickly as possible, and according to what I have said; and place the mires on the pain of the ill limb, then press with the other hand, and stretch it towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if dislocation occurs to the outside, you should not extend the ill leg downward, nor lift him up from the ground, but rather it is best that he remain as if he were already dislocated outside, as we have said on lying on the two haunches; and be laid face down, and the ligament extended as we have said before, and must press firmly on the joint at the table; and will be at a point when the ill patient extends his legs, and they become even; then add the stirrups, and apply the poultice, and the straining bandage of a strip, so that the hunchback does not move; and if he rests for three days or four, then he releases it, and applies the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, as before, then let him rest, three days; then release him, and make him walk well, until his limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The groin is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward, but not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his knee to his groin, and if it does not settle there, know that he is dislocated; and for restoring all of these things, one must seat the patient upright, and extend his leg if possible, and place your back on his face, and put your foot on yours; then take his groin in your hands, and press between your two fingers, then bend both sides of the groin together; and another attendant extends his foot, until the groin returns to its place, and the signs are that he has settled his knee lightly; and apply a plaster, and dry the leg to the groin, and all of the limbs together for three days or four, then release him; and do not let the patient walk, until the members are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not at all moved, extend them greatly, as we have said in the treatment of the gout, until they become healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are sometimes swollen and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that if the ankle is swollen and the joint extends before it becomes dislocated: the limbs should be extended lightly, and one must extend them lightly with the hands when they are only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, it is advisable to sit the patient upright, and tie his leg firmly above the ankle; then take hold of the foot with your right hand, and then again with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and pour the foot into its place with great force; do this twice, as we have said, pouring in and pulling out the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, since it will come back, put the patient to lie on his back on the earth, and firmly fix a stick between his knees, and tie ropes around him so that he does not bleed from the knee; then tighten the tendons of the knee, and other ministers extend the foot to his hands or to its binding, as if it were tied above the neck of the foot; then stretch each minister equally, and the stick will be between the knees of the patient to hold him when one is extending; then put the mires (ligaments) equal to the dislocation in his hands, and other ministers stretch the healthy leg downward, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, and he puts the plaster and poultices on top of it, and the swelling forms, and ties the leg to the thigh, and warms the nerves that are above the ankle so they do not become too strained; then he lets him rest for two or three days, and if the swelling does not subside, he re-applies the poultice; then he releases it on the fourth day or a quarter, and warns the patient to go by four days; and if he goes beyond that term, it is no safety that he will still swell again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the foot, it is to be calmed, as we have said elsewhere, until it is cured.
des dois	of both sides
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they must certainly be extended with labor, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no particular direction of the back or foot, they must certainly be placed on a long table either above it on the left side or above it on the right side; and put your foot under what opens from these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until he is level; and when it is equal, and there is nothing open, place the heel of the foot on two fingers, then tighten them up, and leave it for three days, then release it; and let him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you attempt to restore it, many patients die; so be not presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have used it long enough, and if you are not pitiful or merciful and delay treatment, do not force it; use at the beginning of things cauterizing the abscess deeply, and let the patient fall into the hands of God, if you do not see any chance of recovery; and when you see a chance of recovery, now straighten the member in its place, as soon as the abscess heals; and when the member is in its place, administer gentle cauterizing and heal the wound, as it seems proper, with dry bandages; and if with the dislocation there is breakage and small bones splintered, bind them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will be yours in measure according to your Creator, and because of the wisdom armed with you and your body.
